801 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


In re Appeal of Culp


No. 247 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


104 Pa. Commw. 635; 522 A.2d 1176; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2030


December 19, 1986, Submitted on Briefs  
March 17, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, in case of Re: Appeal of Robert Culp from Decision of Hearing Officer of January 7, 1985, concerning denial of certificate of registration and cease and desist order concerning Mobile Home Park by Bucks County Department of Health on Tax Parcels 12-8-21-1 and 12-8-21-2, Docket No. 85-217-03-6.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mobile home park owner challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed appellee Department of Health's decision to deny appellant's application for a certificate of registration for the mobile home park.


OVERVIEW: After receiving complaints about the operation of a mobile home park, appellee Department of Health informed appellant mobile home park owner that the park was in violation of health regulations, which would have to be met before the park could be certified as required by law. When appellant did not conform to the regulations, appellee issued a cease and desist order. Appellee's hearing officer affirmed the denial of appellant's application for a certificate of registration, as did the lower court. The court held that, under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 16, § 12010, appellee had the authority to make and enforce regulations about public health and safety. There was substantial evidence of deficiencies in the sewer system, the water supply, and the electrical system. These deficiencies created a nuisance and justified appellee's denial of the certificate. In its current state, the park was not a permissible nonconforming use because conformity to the regulations would not prevent appellant from continuing to run the park. Nor was appellee enforcing an ex post facto law. The court held that the regulations were not subject ex post facto analysis, which applied only to criminal statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that denied appellant mobile home park owner a certificate of registration. A commonwealth statute gave appellee Department of Health the authority to issue a cease and desist order for appellant's failure to comply with health regulations. Appellee's order was supported by substantial evidence in the record. Appellant did not have a nonconforming use.

 

802 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Nalbone v. Youngsville


Nos. 3418 C.D. 1985, 3419 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


104 Pa. Commw. 623; 522 A.2d 1173; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2015; 93 Oil & Gas Rep. 537


October 9, 1986, Argued  
March 16, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Warren County, in case of John J. Nalbone, Jr., and Louis J. Nalbone v. Borough of Youngsville, No. 276 of 1985.



DISPOSITION: Appeal No. 3418 C.D. 1985 -- Order reversed and remanded. Appeal No. 3419 C.D. 1985 quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Warren County (Pennsylvania), which on its own motion granted summary judgment in favor of appellee Borough of Youngsville, Pennsylvania, found that appellee's ordinances were a legal exercise of police power, and further denied appellants' motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowners wanted to drill oil and/or gas wells upon their property, but were prevented from doing so by the operation of two ordinances enacted by appellee Borough of Youngsville, Pennsylvania. Appellants challenged the validity of the ordinances in the trial court and asserted that the Oil and Gas Act, 58 P.S. § 601.101 to .605, had preempted the field of oil and gas mine regulation so as to supersede local efforts to so regulate, and that the ordinances were confiscatory and, thus, unconstitutional because they effectively acted to deprive appellants of their property without due process of law. The trial court on its own motion granted summary judgment to appellee, and found that the ordinances were a legal exercise of police power enacted for the preservation of the health, safety, and general welfare of its residents. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded because no evidence was submitted on whether appellants' property rights were abridged, so there was a genuine issue of fact for the trial court to resolve, notwithstanding the court's finding that the ordinances were reasonable and validly promulgated under the Pennsylvania Municipalities Planning Code.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee Borough of Youngsville, Pennsylvania and remanded for consideration of the factual issues raised in appellant property owners' complaint because no evidence was submitted on whether appellants' property rights were abridged, so a genuine issue of fact existed for the trial court to resolve.

 

803 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Guy v. Woods


No. 1649 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


104 Pa. Commw. 585; 522 A.2d 193; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2011


October 7, 1986, Argued  
March 13, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in the case of Marie Guy v. Robert B. Woods, President of Council, Clinton L. Childs, Jr., Vice-President of Council, Jean L. George, Councilman, James K. Maloney, Councilman, Louis M. Tarasi, Jr., Councilman, Charles E. Throne, Jr., Councilman, Richard E. White, Councilman, James R. Yanckello, Councilman, and Borough of Sewickley, No. GD 80-14935.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant elected member sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed her amended petition for declaratory judgment that challenged the validity of the Council's Rule of Government 2E.


OVERVIEW: Appellant elected member challenged the validity of Council's Rule of Government 2E, which granted discretion to appellees, council and individual members, to close committee meetings to other non-committee members, borough officials and/or the public. Appellant alleged that Rule 2E was unconstitutional, and that the various appellees impermissibly excluded her from committee meetings where she was not a designated member, in violation of rights granted her by U.S. Const. amend. I, XIV. The court affirmed the denial of appellant's declaratory judgment action, and held that because Rule 2E advanced a legitimate government interest and restricted appellant's right to speak and associate in only limited circumstances, it did not violate her U.S. Const. amend. I, XIV rights. Furthermore, the court held that it could see no less restrictive alternative that would effect the local government's end. The court held that Rule 2E comported with the constitutional guarantees of equal protection of the laws and that the classification between committee members and non-committee members arose from a compelling need for the smooth operation of governments at the local level.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant elected member's declaratory judgment action that challenged the validity of a local rule that prohibited appellant from attending various council meetings. The court held that there was no blanket exclusion of non-committee members from committee sessions, and the discretion to close sessions of council was narrowly limited to committee meetings where no formal action could be taken.

 

804 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Barner v. Juniata County Tax Claim Bureau


No. 1728 C.D. 1984


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


104 Pa. Commw. 468; 522 A.2d 169; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1997


July 23, 1986, Submitted on Briefs  
March 10, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied 8/27/87.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Juniata County in the case of Stanley C. Barner, II. and Julia B. Barner v. Juniata County Tax Claim Bureau; Walker Township, Juniata County, Board of Supervisors; Juniata County School Board, No. 433 of 1982.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Juniata County (Pennsylvania), which found in favor of appellees, tax claim bureau, township, county board, and school board, in appellants' action to enjoin appellees from selling appellants' properties in a tax sale due to appellants' failure to pay their real estate taxes in full.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers sought to enjoin a tax sale of their properties due to their refusal to pay the full amount of real estate taxes. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of appellees, tax claim bureau, township, county board, and school board. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellants' request for a continuance at trial because appellants made no showing at the time that the testimony of three missing witnesses would have been more than cumulative of other witnesses' testimony concerning the adequacy of police protection in the area of appellants' properties, or that the testimony of the missing witnesses would have affected the result. The court also held that Pa. R. Civ. P. 212 did not require the trial court to hold a pre-trial conference with appellants in attendance because appellants' counsel was present. The court also found that 72 P.S. § 4692, which exempted veterans from real estate tax liability, was constitutional, and that appellants made no showing that they were entitled to a tax-exempt status. The court determined that appellants' tax liability was ascertainable and payable in United States currency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for appellees, tax claim bureau, township, county board, and school board, in appellant taxpayers' action to enjoin a tax sale of their properties. Appellants were not entitled to a continuance because they did not show that missing witnesses' testimony would not be cumulative. Appellants' presence at a pre-trial conference was not required. Appellants did not show that they should be exempt from paying taxes.

 

805 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


State Conference of State Police Lodges of Fraternal Order of Police v. Commonwealth


No. 3428 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


104 Pa. Commw. 447; 522 A.2d 136; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1994; 125 L.R.R.M. 2736


September 8, 1986, Argued  
March 9, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Jurisdiction in the case of State Conference of State Police Lodges of the Fraternal Order of Police, by its Trustee Ad Litem, Paul T. McCommons v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained and case dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner police union asked the court to exercise its original jurisdiction to declare 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5955 of the State Employees' Retirement Code unconstitutional. Respondent commonwealth filed preliminary objections to the petition for review.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner union was the certified bargaining representative for the state police. The union asked respondent commonwealth to bargain over state police pension benefits pursuant to 43 P.S. §§ 217.1-217.27 (Act 111). Respondent refused and argued that 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5955 of the State Employees' Retirement Code prohibited bargaining over pension issues. Petitioner claimed that reading § 5955 to prohibit discussion of pensions in the collective bargaining process and also to prevent binding arbitration meant that the section was invalid as a special law regulating labor in violation of Pa. Const. art. III, § 32(7) and that the section conflicted with Pa. Const. art. III, § 31. In dismissing petitioner's complaint, the court held that § 5955 effected no discrimination against state police with respect to collective bargaining as to pensions or as to binding arbitration concerning pension legislation, and that the prohibition against special laws did not prohibit the differentiation between state and municipal police with regard to pension entitlement.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the suit for declaratory judgment filed by petitioner police union. The court ruled that the challenged section of the retirement code was not unconstitutional as it effected no discrimination against state police with respect to collective bargaining as to pensions or as to binding arbitration concerning pension legislation, nor was it invalid as a special law.

 

806 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Goodheart v. Thornburgh


No. 3255 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


104 Pa. Commw. 385; 522 A.2d 125; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2002


February 25, 1987, Argued  
March 6, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of Bernard J. Goodheart, et al. v. The Honorable Dick Thornburgh, in his capacity as Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, the General Assembly of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, The State Employees' Retirement Board, and R. Budd Dwyer, in his capacity as Treasurer of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections of General Assembly and Treasurer sustained. Preliminary objections of State Employees' Retirement Board overruled and Board directed to file answer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner judges asked the court to declare unconstitutional portions of the State Employees' Retirement Code of 1974, 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 5101-5956 (1974). Petitioners also sought writs of mandamus against respondents, state employees' retirement board, treasurer, governor, and general assembly. All but the respondent governor filed special exceptions.


OVERVIEW: The Retirement Code of 1959, 71 P.S. §§ 1725-101--1725-809 established a mandatory retirement system for state employees, including judges. In addition to mandatory contributions to the system judges could elect "Class E-1" coverage, which permitted them to contribute a higher percentage of their salaries and receive proportionately higher benefits. The State Employees' Retirement Code of 1974, 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 5101-5956, eliminated Class E-1coverage, however, judges who assumed office before 1974 could continue to elect the Class E-1 coverage. Petitioner judges argued that the duties and responsibilities of judges assuming office before and after 1974 were identical and that the changes established an arbitrary classification based solely on date of entry into judicial service. In overruling the preliminary objections filed by respondent, the state employees' retirement board, the court found that it could not say with absolute certainty that the facts pleaded, if proven, would be insufficient to establish any right to relief under the equal protection or judicial impairment theories that petitioners put forth.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the preliminary objections of respondents, state treasurer and general assembly, to the petition for mandamus filed by petitioner judges and ruled that mandamus could only be ordered if the statute were declared unconstitutional. The court overruled the preliminary objections of respondent state employees' retirement board on the ground that the facts pleaded could establish a right to relief.

CRH Catering Co. v. Commonwealth


No. 2630 C.D. 1983


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


104 Pa. Commw. 91; 521 A.2d 497; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1939


November 17, 1986, Argued  
February 18, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue in the case of In Re: CRH Catering Company, Inc., Docket No. RST-6252, dated August 23, 1983.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer challenged an order of the Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania), which sustained a tax assessment issued by respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania pursuant to 72 P.S. § 7202(d), on food items dispensed by vending machines owned by petitioner.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner taxpayer was an owner of automatic vending machines and was accessed a sales tax by respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania pursuant to 72 P.S. § 7202(d). The state finance board sustained the tax assessment. 72 P.S. § 7204(29), provided an exemption for the sale of food and beverages for human consumption but excluded cafes and other eating-places from the exemption. On appeal the court affirmed the board because a vending machine was more like a restaurant than a grocery store. The court held that the legislature had wide discretion in matters of taxation and the disparate treatment of prepackaged food items did not violate the equal protection clause, U.S. Const. amend XIV, or the Uniformity Clause, Pa. Const. art. VIII, § I.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the state finance board in favor of the respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and against petitioner taxpayer and held that prepackaged vending machine food and beverages were subject to taxation.

 

808 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


First Nat'l Bank v. Commonwealth


No. 562 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


103 Pa. Commw. 337; 520 A.2d 895; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1887


September 10, 1986, Argued  
January 27, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue in the case of In Re: First National Bank of Fredericksburg, Docket No. R-8481, dated February 1, 1985.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner bank sought review of a decision of respondent Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania), which refused its petition for review of resettlement of single excise tax, as settled by the Pennsylvania Department of Revenue and approved by the department of auditor general. Petitioner claimed that the tax in question violated due process and the separation of powers doctrine.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner bank challenged the resettlement of a single excise tax, as settled by respondent Pennsylvania Board of Finance and Revenue concerning the computation of such tax on stocks, bonds, notes, etc. Petitioner claimed that when the department computed the amount of bank's shares that a taxpayer bank owed, the department could not have, under 31 U.S.C.S. § 742, considered obligations of the United States owned by the bank. The court held that the single excise tax violated petitioner's right to due process because it attempted to extinguish a cause of action after it had already accrued. The court further held that the single excise tax violated the separation of powers clauses of the U.S. Const. and Pa. Const. Therefore, the court reversed the decision of respondent and remanded the case so that respondent could resettle the tax against petitioner in accordance with its opinion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of respondent Board of Finance and Revenue, which refused petitioner bank's request for review of resettlement of a single excise tax. The court concluded that the single excise tax violated petitioner's right to due process by attempting to extinguish a cause of action after it had accrued. The court also held that such tax violated the separation of power doctrine.

 

809 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


McSwain v. Commonwealth


No. 3009 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


103 Pa. Commw. 326; 520 A.2d 527; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1880


October 8, 1986, Argued  
January 23, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied December 7, 1987; As Amended (12-7-87).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County in the case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, City of Farrell v. Matthew McSwain, No. 22 Summary Appeal, 1984.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed appellant's conviction for violating a city ordinance relating to the certification of rental dwellings.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landlord was convicted of violating a city ordinance relating to certification of rental dwellings. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the trial court was correct in finding that the ordinance was a constitutional exercise of the city's police power, and that the appellant failed to carry his burden of proving otherwise. The court found that here there was no unreasonable restriction on appellant's right to use his property. Thus, no due process violation occurred. It was reasonable to require frequent inspections of only those dwellings occupied by lessees, especially in light of evidence adduced at trial showing more safety and health problems with those dwellings. Because there was a rational basis for the distinction between rental property and owner-occupied property, there was no equal protection violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant landlord's conviction for violation of a city ordinance relating to the certification of rental dwellings because there was no unreasonable restriction on appellant's use of his property.

 

810 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Tid Bit Alley, Inc. v. Erie County


No. 1058 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


103 Pa. Commw. 46; 520 A.2d 70; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1847


October 10, 1986, Argued  
January 8, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, in case of Erie County, Erie County Department of Health v. Tid Bit Alley, Inc., No. 80-1985.



DISPOSITION: Order modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County (Pennsylvania), which upheld appellee department of health's attempt at regulation controlling the retail sale of bulk food and its enforcement against appellant's method of selling bulk food. Appellant also sought review of the trial court's categorization of appellant's bulk food sale process as a nuisance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation operated a retail food establishment in which it sold bulk food through the use of dispensing containers. The dispensers permitted customer contact with food offered for sale to the public. Appellee department of health adopted a regulation, which was the same as a state regulation by the department of environmental resources (DER). In an equity action, appellee asserted that appellant was required to obtain a license from appellee, and the trial court agreed. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, but as modified. The court found that appellee did not promulgate a county counterpart of the state regulation, 25 Pa. Code § 151.171, with legal effect because it did not follow the necessary steps required to promulgate regulation. However, appellee did have licensing authority under 25 Pa. Code § 151, and it could have prohibited appellant from dispensing bulk foods and could have withheld a license. The court did not find, as the trial court did, that appellant's method of merchandising was a nuisance by statutory definition. Appellant had to stop its current manner of operation until it obtained a license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as modified the judgment of the trial court, which upheld appellee department of health's attempt at regulation controlling the retail sale of bulk food and its enforcement against appellant corporation's method of selling bulk food. Although appellee's attempt at adopting a regulation was unsuccessful, appellee had the authority to regulate the manner in which appellant sold its bulk food through appellee's licensing power.

Commonwealth by Zimmerman v. Nat'l Apt. Leasing Co.


No. 185 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


102 Pa. Commw. 623; 519 A.2d 1050; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2719


October 8, 1986, Argued  
December 30, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania by Attorney General LeRoy S. Zimmerman, Plaintiff v. National Apartment Leasing Company a/k/a NALCO, Defendant.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained in part and overruled in part. Complainant granted leave to file amended complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landlord filed preliminary objections to the complaint filed by plaintiff attorney general under § 4 of the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law, 73 P.S. § 201-4.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff attorney general filed suit against defendant landlord pursuant to § 4 of the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law (Law), 73 P.S. § 201-4. The complaint accused defendant of withholding from its renters' security deposits a sum, which the renters claimed to have been exorbitant as a charge for cleaning services to rehabilitate the rented premises upon termination of the lease. Plaintiff filed preliminary objections to the complaint which raised a question of jurisdiction, sought to strike scandalous and impertinent material, sought a more specific pleading, demurred to the complaint, and raised the defenses of lack of capacity to sue and lis pendens. In sustaining in part and overruling in part the objections and in granting plaintiff leave to file an amended complaint, the court held that it had proper jurisdiction over the matter. However, it found that plaintiff failed to plead any alleged fraud with particularity as required by Pa. R. Civ. P. 1019(b) and that the complaint failed to make out a cause of action such as was authorized by the Law. It therefore sustained defendant's motion for a more specific pleading and its demurrer.


OUTCOME: The court sustained in part and overruled in part the preliminary objections of defendant landlord to the complaint filed by plaintiff attorney general. The court found that plaintiff failed to plead fraud with the required particularity and that the complaint failed to make out a cause of action such as was authorized by the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law. The court granted defendant leave to file an amended complaint.

 

812 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth, Dep't of Transp. v. Consolidated Rail Corp.


No. 1634 C.D. 1985, No. 1829 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


102 Pa. Commw. 611; 519 A.2d 1058; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2721


October 8, 1986, Argued  
December 29, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in the case of Consolidated Rail Corporation v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Transportation, No. GD 81-30367.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state transportation department and appellee railroad sought review of an order of the Allegheny County Common Pleas Court (Pennsylvania), which denied post-trial motions based on immunity and damages under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8528, entering judgment for appellee in its negligent highway maintenance action against appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellee railroad filed an action against appellant state transportation department, alleging that appellant's negligent failure to maintain the drainage structures along the highway caused the landslide that destabilized appellee's railroad tracks and resulted in a train wreck. The lower court found appellant negligent, awarding delay damages and the maximum statutory damages under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8528 to appellee. Both parties filed post-trial motions for judgment, which were denied. Appellee challenged the lower court's order, attacking the constitutionality of the statutory damage limit and the calculation of delay damages. Appellant claimed that its negligence was not established and that appellee's failure to give notice under § 8528 precluded liability. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, concluding that there was no error or discretionary abuse in the lower court's denial of either party's post-trial motions because the damage limits were constitutional, and delay damages were properly based on the statutory limit. Moreover, appellant's negligence was established and the exception to immunity under § 8528 did not require notice of liability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, which denied post-trial motions based on sovereign immunity and damages and entered judgment for appellee railroad in its negligent highway maintenance action against appellant state transportation department. The court held that negligence was established, that notice was not required, that statutory damages limits were constitutional, and that delay damages were properly calculated.

 

813 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Cloonan v. Thornburgh


No. 3467 C.D. 1986, No. 3481 C.D. 1986, No. 3534 C.D. 1986, No. 3535 C.D. 1986, No. 3604 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


103 Pa. Commw. 1; 519 A.2d 1040; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2725


December 22, 1986, Heard  
December 29, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of Edward A. Cloonan v. The Honorable Dick Thornburgh, Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board v. Governor Richard Thornburgh; Wendell W. Young, Individually, as a taxpayer et al. v. Governor Dick Thornburgh; Edward P. Zemprelli et al. v. Dick Thornburgh; and United Food and Commercial Workers Local 1357 et al. v. Governor Richard Thornburgh.



DISPOSITION: Application by the Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board for summary relief granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board and store representatives filed seven separate applications for special and preliminary relief involving five actions brought against respondent Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, arising from his issuance of an order providing for the phase-out of petitioner Liquor Control Board.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania issued an order which provided for the phase-out of petitioner Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board (PCLB) by December 31, 1986 under the guise of the Sunset Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 71, §§ 1795.1 to 1795.14. Petitioner PCLB, along with petitioner store representatives, sought summary relief in having the Sunset Act declared unconstitutional, enjoining the implementation of respondent's order, and having the court define the legal status of petitioner PLCB after December 31, 1986. The court granted summary relief for petitioners, though it found that the Sunset Act was constitutional, because in the enactment, all legislative procedural constitutional requirements were met. The order of respondent, however, was held to be null and void. Because it was in direct conflict with provisions in the Sunset Act, the court found that it wrongfully invaded the exclusive province of the General Assembly to control every phase of the alcoholic beverage industry and was therefore invalid. Petitioner PLCB was allowed to continue operating for an extended period of time but was still ordered to wind up its affairs by June 30, 1987.


OUTCOME: The court found that the order of respondent Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania was in conflict with the Sunset Act and was thus invalid. The Sunset Act was held to be constitutional, and summary relief was granted to petitioners, Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board and store representatives, because respondent's order invaded the exclusive province of the General Assembly to control every phase of the alcoholic beverage industry.

 

814 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Rodebaugh


No. 3399 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


102 Pa. Commw. 592; 519 A.2d 555; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2717


September 12, 1986, Argued  
December 24, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Board of Claims in case of Everett G. Rodebaugh and Grace H. Rodebaugh, h/w v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, No. FC-192-80, dated November 21, 1985.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner commonwealth sought review of a decision from the Board of Claims (Pennsylvania) which found in favor of respondent claimant and awarded her judgment against petitioner for its failure to comply with the statement of principles which accompanied a charitable donation of land given for use by a state college.


OVERVIEW: Respondent claimant donated a large estate to petitioner commonwealth for use by West Chester State College. Accompanying the conveyance was a statement of principles in which petitioner agreed to furnish full and first-class maintenance of the residence, contents, and grounds according to standards as previously observed, casualty and liability insurance, and security service. At first, petitioner fulfilled the terms of the statement, but it eventually breached the agreement when the General Assembly denied its funding. Respondent then was forced to fund the maintenance and upkeep and pay the insurance premiums on the estate. Upon her claim to recover her expenditures, the Board of Claims found in her favor. Petitioner appealed, but the court affirmed the board's decision after its limited review to determine whether necessary factual findings were supported by substantial evidence and whether an error of law was committed. The court found that the agreement which accompanied the conveyance was a binding contract and petitioner had breached its terms. The award to refund the insurance premiums was also proper because respondent had an insurable interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board of Claims' decision in all respects. In its holding it found that the statement of principles, which accompanied a charitable donation of land and was agreed to by both petitioner commonwealth and respondent claimant, had become a binding contract. Because of petitioner's breach of that contract, the board was correct in awarding respondent expenses, including insurance premiums, and interest.

 

815 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Reichard-Coulston, Inc. v. Revenue Appeals Bd.


No. 1110 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


102 Pa. Commw. 227; 517 A.2d 1372; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2682


September 9, 1986, Argued  
November 17, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County in the case of Reichard-Coulston, Inc. v. Revenue Appeals Board, Northampton County, No. 1983-C-8320.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a decision of the Northampton County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which established an assessment value of certain property belonging to appellant. Appellant claimed that the lower court erred in relying on the cost approach in determining the market value of the property in question.


OVERVIEW: Respondent county revenue appeals board assessed certain property owned by appellant corporation, which had been improved throughout several years. Appellant sought de novo review in the lower court concerning respondent's assessment. The lower court concluded that the "cost approach" was the correct method by which to value the property; thus, respondent's assessment was upheld. Appellant challenged the decision and alleged that the market data approach was the correct method to value its property. The court affirmed. The court held that the lower court judge committed no error in his consideration of the cost approach, and it concluded that no abuse of discretion was committed in the lower court judge's particular application of it in appellant's case. The court noted that 72 P.S. § 5348(d) afforded respondent and the lower court with a choice as to how to value the property. Therefore, the court held that the lower court, in choosing the cost approach, did not abuse its discretion; thus, the lower court's decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court that established the assessment value of certain property owned by appellant corporation. The court held that the lower court did not abuse its discretion in adopting the cost approach in determining the assessment, instead of using the market data approach.

 

816 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Bloomingdale's by Mail, Ltd. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Revenue


No. 2345 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


101 Pa. Commw. 431; 516 A.2d 827; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2615


September 10, 1986, Argued  
October 22, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in case of Bloomingdale's By Mail, Ltd. v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Revenue, and James I. Scheiner, in his capacity as Secretary of Revenue, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Revenue.



DISPOSITION: Motion for summary judgment denied. Writs quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, Department of Revenue, filed a motion for partial summary judgment seeking a determination as to whether it could compel petitioner, a mail order retailer, to provide respondent with mail order transactional sales data concerning petitioner's customers who purchased items subject to the Pennsylvania use tax. Petitioner filed a declaratory judgment action to which respondent answered and filed its own declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, department of revenue, filed a motion for partial summary judgment seeking a determination as to whether it could compel petitioner, a mail order retailer, to provide respondent with mail order transactional sales data concerning its customers who purchased items subject to the Pennsylvania use tax. Petitioner originally filed a declaratory judgment action seeking a declaration that it was not obligated to provide the data to respondent. Respondent answered and filed its own declaratory judgment action. The court denied respondent's motion for partial summary judgment, holding that, as a matter of law, respondent's subpoena power did not extend beyond the borders of the commonwealth. Respondent, through the use of administrative writs, attempted to compel the presence of witnesses and the production of documents that were outside the commonwealth. Respondent was bound by the restrictions in § 1602 of the Fiscal Code, 72 P.S. § 1602, and could not exercise powers not explicitly granted to it by the legislature. The court quashed respondent's administrative writs.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion for partial summary judgment filed by respondent, department of revenue, and quashed respondent's administrative writs that sought to compel petitioner, a mail order retailer, to provide it with transactional sales data concerning items subject to the Pennsylvania use tax. The court held that respondent's subpoena power did not extend beyond the borders of the commonwealth.

 

817 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Stajkowski v. Carbon County Bd. of Assessment & Revision of Taxes


No. 29 T.D. 1984


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


101 Pa. Commw. 207; 515 A.2d 1035; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2586


June 3, 1985, Argued  
October 6, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued April 9, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Carbon County in the case of Father Leo Stajkowski v. Carbon County Board of Assessment and Revision of Taxes, No. 83 S 91.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant clergyman sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Carbon County (Pennsylvania), which denied his appeal from a decision of respondent board of assessment. Appellant contended the occupational assessment classification and tax as it applied to clergymen violated his right to free exercise of his religion pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Appellant clergyman sought review of an order, which denied his appeal from a decision of respondent board of assessment. Appellant contended the occupational assessment classification and tax as it applied to clergymen violated his right to free exercise of his religion pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. I. Appellant argued that because the occupational classification of "clergyman" was undefined it operated to tax all of his activities including his religious ones, hence violating his right to free exercise of religion. On appeal the court stated that in a free exercise case, it was necessary for one to show the coercive effect of the enactment as it operated against him in the practice of his religion. The court found no hint that the tax had had a coercive effect upon appellant in the practice of his religion. At no point did appellant state that the tax prevented him from carrying out his religious practices or penalized him for his faith. Nor did appellant state that he was unable to pay the assessment because it was beyond his financial ability to do so. The court affirmed the order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court because the occupational assessment classification and tax as it applied to clergymen did not violate appellant clergyman's right to free exercise of his religion pursuant to the first amendment.

Hummer v. Board of School Directors

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision by the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the demurrer of appellee school district and its Board of School Directors to the appellants' complaint in equity.

The trial court declined to address the issue of the constitutionality of the tax because the complaint did not assert that the tax was unconstitutional. Appellants then sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that appellee had the statutory authority to impose the tax for support of the college, and that because appellants did not raise the issue in their complaint that the tax was unconstitutional, the trial court's refusal to address the constitutional issue was proper.

819 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Electro-Space Fabricators, Inc. v. Commonwealth


No. 3656 C.D. 1983


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


100 Pa. Commw. 74; 514 A.2d 260; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2456


May 13, 1986, Argued  
August 20, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania Board of Finance and Revenue in the case of In Re: Electro-Space Fabricators, Inc., Docket No. R-7322, dated November 29, 1983.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation, appealed the order from respondent Pennsylvania Board of Finance and Revenue which refused to resettle petitioner's capital stock tax liability for the year in dispute and refused to allow petitioner to use the three factor apportionment method set forth in Article IV of the Tax Reform Code of 1971, Pa. Stat. tit. 72, §§ 7401-7412.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner corporation was incorporated in the state and conducted all of its business from its headquarters in the state. During the disputed tax year, petitioner was not subject to a net income tax, franchise tax, or corporate stock tax in any other state. Respondent Pennsylvania Board of Finance refused to calculate petitioner's capital stock tax liability for the disputed year using the three factor apportionment method from Article IV of the Tax Reform Code of 1971, Pa. Stat. tit. 72, §§ 7401-7412. Petitioner appealed to the court challenging respondent's refusal. The sole issue before the court was whether petitioner, a domestic corporation which was not subject to tax in any state except Pennsylvania, could elect to use the three factor apportionment method to determine its tax liability under the capital stock tax. The court ruled that under the relevant case law, petitioner was prohibited from using the three factor method, regardless of why it was using the method. Since petitioner was not subject to taxation in any other state, it had not met the condition precedent to the use of the three factor method and it was prohibited from using it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from respondent Pennsylvania Board of Finance and Revenue and entered judgment in respondent's favor because the court ruled that petitioner corporation was not entitled to use the three factor apportionment method.

 

820 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Prudential Property & Casualty Ins. Co. v. Muir


No. 1127 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


99 Pa. Commw. 620; 513 A.2d 1129; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2448


April 9, 1986, Argued  
August 13, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania Insurance Commissioner in the case of In Re: Prudential Property and Casualty Insurance Company, Docket No. R84-3-1.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insurance company appealed an order of the Pennsylvania Insurance Commissioner which affirmed a decision of the Insurance Department of Pennsylvania disapproving petitioner's policy form filings deleting or modifying the uninsured motorist arbitration clause. Petitioner challenged commissioner's authority to promulgate the regulation found at 31 Pa. Code § 63.2(a) and argued that arbitration denied it the right to a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner insurance company appealed an order of the Insurance Commissioner of Pennsylvania (Commissioner) which affirmed a decision of the Insurance Department of Pennsylvania disapproving petitioner's policy form filings deleting or modifying the uninsured motorist arbitration clause. The Commissioner's order was based on his conclusion that the regulation found at 31 Pa. Code § 63.2(a) required the arbitration clause which petitioner sought to delete or modify be a part of an automobile insurance policy providing uninsured motorist coverage. Petitioner argued that the commissioner did not have authority to promulgate the regulation and argued that arbitration denied it the right to a jury trial. The court, affirming the Commissioner's order, held that the Insurance Department had the authority to promulgate a regulation requiring an arbitration clause in an insurance contract because it had a statutory duty to enforce the regulation. The court stated that Pa. Const. art. I, § 6 did not provide for a jury trial for uninsured motorist coverage and therefore there could be no violation of the constitutional right to a jury trial by requiring such binding arbitration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Insurance Commissioner's order, finding that the Insurance Department had the implied authority to promulgate the regulation in questions, which authority was derived from the statutory duty to enforce the statute by approving policies which provided proper protection to victims of uninsured motorist. The court stated that there was no violation of a right to a jury trial because it was not contained in the statute.

West v. Township Supervisors of Adams Township


No. 3308 C.D. 1984


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


99 Pa. Commw. 599; 513 A.2d 1114; 513 A.2d 1120; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2445


March 12, 1986, Argued  
August 12, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Butler County in the case of James A. West v. Township Supervisors of Adams Township, Stanley Wilhelm and Clara Wilhelm, Wayne Hindman and Pat Hindman, and Thomas Lower and Shirley Lower, No. 80-726, Book 119, page 61.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated. Ordinance declared invalid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Butler County (Pennsylvania), in favor of appellee township, which ruled that the area in which appellant wanted to build a mobile home park was not in the logical path for growth and development.


OVERVIEW: Appellant developer challenged appellee township's zoning ordinance, which entirely excluded mobile home parks and all other multifamily uses from the municipality. The trial court determined on the basis of the substantial evidence that the municipality was not a logical area for development and growth, and ruled against appellant. Appellant sought review. The court vacated the order, and ruled that appellant could proceed with the proposed development, subject to all other reasonable zoning and other applicable laws. The court held that nothing on the record provided the justification for the total exclusion of mobile home parks and other multifamily uses from the entire municipality; thus, appellee failed to sustain the burden of justifying that exclusion. The court concluded that a fair share analysis was not required to assess the exclusionary impact of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order, which found that the proposed area was not a logical path for development, and held that appellee township failed to sustain its burden of justifying an ordinance that completely excluded mobile home parks from the municipality.

 

822 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Quality Markets, Inc. v. Commonwealth


No. 1692 C.D. 1984


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


99 Pa. Commw. 537; 514 A.2d 228; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2433


February 5, 1986, Argued  
August 8, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue in the case of In Re: Quality Markets, Inc., Docket No. C-12,883, dated May 29, 1984.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer sought review of an order from the Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania), which refused a petition for refund of franchise tax for the year ending January 30, 1982.


OVERVIEW: The Board of Finance and Revenue refused petitioner taxpayer's petition for refund of franchise tax for the year ending January 30, 1982. Petitioner was incorporated under the laws of the State of New York, and was engaged in the operation of retail grocery stores located in both New York and the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. The issue on appeal was whether a foreign corporation which elected to be taxed under the single-factor apportionment formula could be required to include its intangible assets in the computation of its franchise tax due. The court stated that because petitioner was afforded an option to choose between the single-factor and three-factor formulas, it was this option that had to be scrutinized, as a whole, to determine it if passed constitutional muster. The court held that this option, as applied to petitioner, was constitutional. The court concluded that the option to choose between the single-factor and three-factor tax formulas, as afforded to foreign corporations, met the requirements of the Due Process Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, and the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. The court affirmed the Board's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Board of Finance and Revenue, which refused a petition for refund of franchise tax. Petitioner's option to choose between the single-factor and three-factor apportionment formulas met the requirements of the Due Process Clause and the Commerce Clause.

Sheakley v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Transp.


No. 289 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


99 Pa. Commw. 328; 513 A.2d 551; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2405


June 12, 1986, Submitted on Briefs  
July 30, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied June 1, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Deborah Anne Sheakley, No. S.A. No. 550 of 1984.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) that dismissed appellant's challenge of the suspension of her driver's license by the Pennsylvania Department of Transportation after a de novo hearing.


OVERVIEW: After appellant driver refused to submit to a breathalyzer test, the Pennsylvania Department of Transportation suspended her driver's license for one year pursuant to the Implied Consent Law (law), 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1547. The trial court dismissed the initial appeal and appellant sought further review. Appellant contended that her due process and equal protection rights were violated when the arresting officer failed to give her adequate warnings of the results of her refusal. The court noted that operating a motor vehicle upon the highways was not a civil or property right but was rather a privilege subject to the commonwealth's regulation and control. The court held that the privilege of operating a motor vehicle was not entitled to strict constitutional protection and that the conditions imposed by the commonwealth upon the use of the privilege were only required to bear a rational relationship to a legitimate state objective. The court held that the law in question bore a rational relationship to the commonwealth's interests in safeguarding the public from injury and death at the hands of intoxicated drivers and affirmed the lower court's dismissal of the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of an appeal of the suspension of appellant's driver's license because it held that the law under which the suspension was imposed bore a rational relationship to the commonwealth's interests in safeguarding the public from injury and death at the hands of intoxicated drivers.

Butler Township Bd. of Supervisors v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Environmental Resources

OVERVIEW: Appellants, city and township board, challenged a decision by the environmental hearing board that dismissed a challenge from an order of respondent department of environmental resources. Respondent required appellant township board and several surrounding municipalities and authorities to enter into an agreement to provide for the construction of a regional sewage treatment plant at a specific site within appellant township board's boundaries. Appellants argued that the environmental harm that would result from the sewage treatment plant outweighed the benefits derived from the plant. Germantown Sav. Bank v. Philadelphia


No. 15 T.D. 1985, No. 9 T.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


98 Pa. Commw. 508; 512 A.2d 756; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2331


April 9, 1986, Argued  
July 7, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, in cases of Germantown Savings Bank v. City of Philadelphia, No. 5803 May Term, 1983 and I.C.S. Corporation v. City of Philadelphia, No. 897 September Term, 1982.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed. Case remanded to Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which determined that appellee city was not liable for any damages to appellants' property to the extent appellants were compensated for their injuries by insurance. The trial court also certified as a controlling question the constitutionality of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 8553(d).


OVERVIEW: Appellants brought separate subrogation actions against appellee city, alleging that appellee's negligence in inspecting and maintaining certain fire hydrants caused the hydrants to rupture and destroy appellants' property. The trial court determined that appellee was not liable for any damages to the extent appellants were compensated for their injuries by insurance. The trial court certified as a controlling question the constitutionality of § 8553(d) of the Political Subdivision Tort Claims Act (Act), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 8553(d). On appeal, the court held that the appropriate level of scrutiny under the equal protection clause to be applied to the matter was the rational relationship test. Further, the court held that classifying plaintiffs who received insurance benefits differently from those plaintiffs who would not receive insurance benefits was rationally related to the legitimate government interest in clearly defining the extent to which a political subdivision was at financial risk. The court concluded that § 8553(d) of the act was not violative of equal protection. The court affirmed the order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings. Appellee city was not liable for any damages to appellants' property to the extent appellants were compensated for their injuries by insurance; the Political Subdivision Tort Claims Act was not violative of equal protection.

Greenstein v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Health


No. 999 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


98 Pa. Commw. 445; 512 A.2d 739; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2328


April 10, 1986, Argued  
July 1, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Department of Health, in case of Sidney Greenstein, M.D., dated March 11, 1985.



DISPOSITION: Case dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner doctor sought review of the decision of respondent Department of Health (Pennsylvania) that approved petitioner's termination as a participating doctor with a health service corporation pursuant to the Professional Health Services Plan Corporations Act, 40 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6324(a). Petitioner alleged that he was unconstitutionally denied a hearing as required by Administrative Agency Law, 2 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 504.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner doctor was a participating doctor with a health service corporation. After receiving several complaints about excessive fees petitioner charged subscribers, the health care corporation issued a complaint and scheduled a hearing. Petitioner did not appear at the hearing. Staino v. Commonwealth, Pennsylvania State Horse Racing Com.


No. 1794 C.D. 1983


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


98 Pa. Commw. 461; 512 A.2d 75; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2329


April 10, 1986, Submitted on Briefs  
July 1, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania State Racing Commission, in case of In Re: Ralph Staino, No. 82-156K.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, patron at a racetrack, appealed from the order of respondent Pennsylvania State Racing Commission that dismissed his appeal after he was ejected from a racetrack by a racing association.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, patron at a racetrack, was ejected by a representative of the racing association. Respondent state racing commission, after a hearing, rejected petitioner's appeal of his ejectment because under Section 215 of the Horse Race Industry Reform Act (Act), 4 Pa. Stat. § 325.215, the racing association's authority to eject patrons from the race track was limited only to the extent that the person may not be ejected because of his race, color, creed, sex, national origin or religion, and petitioner had not established a prima facie case of ejectment for one or more of the prohibited reasons. The court affirmed, holding that the act was unambiguous in its affirmation of the racing association's right to eject petitioner from the racetrack without cause. The court also held that the ejectment was not a state action for purposes of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and that petitioner had no constitutional right to a seat at the racetrack.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed petitioner patron's ejection from the racetrack because the racing association could eject petitioner for no cause, the ejectment did not amount to state action, and petitioner had no constitutional right to a seat at the racetrack.

Lal v. Brooks


No. 3614 C.D. 1984


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


98 Pa. Commw. 380; 511 A.2d 277; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2311


December 12, 1985, Argued  
June 26, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, in case of Amrit Lal, Individually and on behalf of others similarly situated v. Irene B. Brooks, Prothonotary of Chester County, Pennsylvania, No. 84-00824.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania) which sustained the preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer raised by appellee prothonotary, and dismissed appellant's complaint in mandamus.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was sworn into office of county prothonotary on Monday, January 2, 1984. Because New Year's day fell on a Sunday that year, the holiday was observed on Monday, and so, appellee began her commission on a day when all county offices were closed. The following day, January 3, appellee raised filing fees. Appellant filed for a writ of mandamus seeking, inter alia, to compel appellee to reinstate the former fees. On appellee's motion for a demurrer, the trial court sustained appellee's preliminary objections. The appellate court affirmed, holding that appellee raised the filing fee in a timely fashion, despite the provision in 42 P.S. § 21071 that required filing fees to be raised on or before January 1, because under 1 P.S. § 1908, January 1 and January 2 were not counted in determining the time limitation. Further, the court held that it was within appellee's discretion to determine what a reasonable fee was as long as the fee was within the statutory limits, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that appellant had not alleged sufficient facts to support the contention that his constitutional rights were violated.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing appellant's complaint for mandamus was affirmed because the first two days were not counted in determining any time limitation under the statute, and the filing fee was timely. Further, the court held that the fee was presumptively reasonable, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion because appellant failed to allege sufficient facts that his constitutional rights were violated.

 

829 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Fortson v. Commonwealth, Crime Victim's Compensation Bd.


No. 3652 C.D. 1984


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


98 Pa. Commw. 272; 512 A.2d 734; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2295


September 12, 1985, Argued  
June 19, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued May 4, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Crime Victim's Compensation Board in the case of Claimant: Edna F. Fortson, Claim No. 83-0522-D, dated November 7, 1984.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner widow sought review of a decision of respondent Crime Victim's Compensation Board (Pennsylvania), which denied her claim for benefits. Respondent had determined that petitioner was ineligible to receive an award because the total amount payable to her from other sources, counted as an offset for award purposes, exceeded the amount payable to her under the Crime Victim's Compensation Act, 71 P.S. §§ 180-7 to -7.18.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner widow's husband, a deputy sheriff, was killed. She made a claim under the Crime Victim's Compensation Act (Act), 71 P.S. §§ 180-7 to -7.18. Respondent Crime Victim's Compensation Board denied her claim under 71 P.S. § 180-7.9, which required respondent to reduce any potential award by amounts payable to the claimant that the claimant was entitled to receive from other sources as a result of the crime. Respondent included petitioner's deceased's pension benefits in determining that the offset amount exceeded any potential award. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for recomputation. It held that evidence of future earnings and the impact of inflation were not relevant, and that respondent properly ignored these factors in calculating petitioner's potential award under 37 Pa. Code § 191.9b(a). However, respondent had treated the victim's pension as money from public funds under 71 P.S. § 180-7.9(e), which as an offset exceeded petitioner's expenses and loss of support. The court held that the pension was deferred compensation and thus not public funds and therefore not an offset under the Act. The court remanded for a corrected computation of the offset.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of respondent board that petitioner widow was not entitled to compensation from a crime victim's fund. Respondent had properly calculated the loss of support and out-of-pocket expenses but had improperly treated the victim's pension as received from public funds. Since the pension was deferred compensation it was not public funds and hence not an offset. The matter was remanded to recalculate and award benefits.

 

830 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Northeastern Educational Intermediate Unit #19 v. Stephens


No. 1449 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


98 Pa. Commw. 127; 510 A.2d 1267; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2261


November 14, 1985, Argued  
June 12, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued February 5, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County in the case of Donald K. Stephens v. Northeastern Intermediate Unit No. 19, No. 84 Civil 6018.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant educational unit sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County (Pennsylvania), which reversed the decision of the Board of Directors and directed that appellee teacher, a veteran, be reinstated to his teaching position without diminution of his seniority rights and with full backpay.


OVERVIEW: Appellee teacher appealed his furlough maintaining that in computing his seniority for furlough purposes, the Board of Directors (board) of appellant educational unit should have taken into account the time he served in the armed forces pursuant to 51 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7107. The trial court reversed the board's decision and the court affirmed the trial court and determined that the legislature did not preclude the application of § 7107 to 24 P.S. 11-1125.1. The court stated that the school code did not define seniority and that it was reasonable to read § 7107 as supplementing § 1125.1. The court held that appellee met the criteria enunciated in § 7107 because as a public school teacher, he was in a public position, and he was a civil servant. The court held that the compensation of a veteran for the disadvantage he would have suffered due to his exclusion from the labor market by appending his time in the military to his other service when computing seniority for furlough purposes was a reasonable governmental objective with a rational relationship to the method employed, and application of § 7107 in appellee's case withstood constitutional scrutiny.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order and held that Veteran's Preference Act (act), in appellee teacher's case, withstood constitutional scrutiny, and that the legislature had not precluded the application of the act to the school code. The court also found that appellee was within the class the legislature sought to protect when it enacted the act.

 

831 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Welsh


No. 3796 C.D. 1984


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


97 Pa. Commw. 588; 510 A.2d 850; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2227


April 10, 1986, Argued  
June 2, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County in the case of Estate of Edna M. Welsh, Deceased, No. 83802, dated September 20, 1983.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth appealed an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which held that an appraisement was valid and controlling, and that there was no authority for the Department of Revenue, Board of Appeal's decision and ordered the commonwealth to refund appellee executor its overpayment of inheritance tax, plus interest.


OVERVIEW: Appellee executor filed an inheritance tax return and later filed a petition for refund. The commonwealth, through its appraiser, appraised the estate and filed a protest 61 days after receipt of the objected-to notice. The board of appeals subsequently dismissed the commonwealth's protest and found that appellee was entitled to a refund of overpayment of inheritance tax without interest. The commonwealth filed an inheritance tax record adjustment. Appellee sought review and the lower court held that the appraisement was valid and controlling, and that there was no authority for the board's decision. The lower court ordered the commonwealth to refund appellee its overpayment plus interest. The commonwealth appealed and the court affirmed the lower court's decree nisi. The court held that the commonwealth must be bound by its original appraisement taxing the estate left to the step-grandchildren at six percent. To allow the commonwealth to retain the requested refund would have amounted to taxing the estate at 15 percent, something that it is precluded from doing by its failure to take a timely appeal from the original assessment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court that had awarded appellee executor a refund of her overpayment of inheritance tax plus interest. The court held that to allow the commonwealth to retain the requested refund would have amounted to taxing the estate at 15 percent, something that it was precluded from doing by its failure to take a timely appeal from the original assessment.

 

832 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Easton v. Andy's Excavating


No. 1309 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


97 Pa. Commw. 412; 509 A.2d 969; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2203


February 6, 1986, Submitted on Briefs  
May 22, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County, in case of Andy's Excavating, Inc. v. City of Easton and Township of Williams, No. 1982-C-6203.
Andy's Excavating, Inc. v. Easton, 38 Pa. D. & C.3d 498, 1985 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 246 (1985)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County (Pennsylvania), which declared unconstitutional a city ordinance that restricted commercial truck traffic on certain streets in appellee business' action for a declaratory judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city's ordinance that restricted commercial truck traffic did not apply to commercial trucks that had a destination within appellant's limits. Line Street was a boundary line between appellant and a township. Because appellee business was located on the township side of Line Street, and not within appellant's limits, commercial vehicles servicing it could not use Line Street, and the only alternate route was not usable. For those reasons, the lower court declared the ordinance unconstitutional. On review, the court rejected appellant's contention that the trial court's finding of fact about the unsuitability of the alternative route was not supported by substantial evidence because the lower court, the sole judge of credibility, accepted the testimony of appellee's owner. The court also rejected appellant's contention that finding the ordinance unconstitutional was error because that same argument was presented to the lower court and was disposed of in the judge's opinion. Accordingly, the court affirmed the lower court's declaration that appellant's ordinance was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the declaration that appellant city's ordinance restricting commercial truck traffic was unconstitutional. The finding that the alternative route to service appellee business was unusable was supported by substantial evidence because the trial court, the sole judge of credibility, accepted appellee's testimony. The contention that the statute was not unconstitutional was disposed of in the lower court judge's opinion.

Tohickon Valley Transfer, Inc. v. Tinicum Township Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 578 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


97 Pa. Commw. 244; 509 A.2d 896; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2171


April 9, 1986, Argued  
May 15, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, in case of Tri-State Transfer Co., Inc. and Tohickon Valley Transfer, Inc., Thomas L. Treadway and Shirley A. Lojeski v. Tinicum Township Zoning Hearing Board, No. 83-6869-14-5.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, intervenor mortgagee, challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a decision of appellee township's zoning hearing board rejecting the application of corporation, present owner of the site for approval of a trash transfer station.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the trial court's order holding that appellant's, intervenor mortgagee, trash transfer station proposal complied with the use and floodplain restrictions of the zoning ordinance because it fell within an express permitted use category in the industrial district, and its physical structures were proposed to be within a flood plain district. The court found that because the earlier approved permit, as renewed, expired finally before either the present owner or mortgagee acquired any interest, the facts showed no expenditure made on the basis of that permit; therefore, appellant could not claim to have made any expenditure toward establishing a use in reliance upon a permit. The court held that the present proposal came within a permitted use category because the literal terms of the zoning ordinance, relating to the storage and disposition of discarded materials, embraced refuse of all kinds because discarded materials and refuse are synonymous. The court upheld the trial court's finding that the zoning hearing board erred when it misinterpreted the floodplain zoning provisions and map because there was no legal basis for that conclusion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order affirming the decision of appellee township's zoning hearing board rejecting corporation's application for approval of a trash transfer station. The court held that the trash station proposal complied with the use and floodplain restrictions because it fell within an express permitted use category in the industrial district, and its physical structures were proposed to be within a floodplain district.

Formicola v. Workmen's Compensation Appeal Bd. (Philadelphia)


No. 2725 C.D. 1983


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


97 Pa. Commw. 274; 509 A.2d 434; 1986 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2172


December 9, 1985, Argued  
May 15, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board, in case of Anna Formicola w/o Philip v. City of Philadelphia, No. A-85386.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner widow appealed from a decision of respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a referee's denial of her fatal claim petition on the basis of 77 P.S. § 411(1). Petitioner's spouse was a police officer who suffered a myocardial infarction while on duty and died 13 years later, well after the automatic 300 week limitation for claims on death for compensation provided for in § 411(1).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner widow sought review from a decision of respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board denying her fatal claim petition on the basis of 77 P.S. § 411(1), of the Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Act (Act). Petitioner's spouse had been a police officer who suffered a myocardial infarction while on duty and died 13 years later, well after the automatic 300-week limitation for claims under the Act. The court affirmed respondent's decision and concluded that the Act did not violate either due process or equal protection. The court stated that it could not say the time limitation was unreasonable, and therefore, it did not find any due process violation. The court rejected petitioner's argument that by including certain instances of heart disease to firemen within the category of occupational disease and not similarly including such instances to policemen, the legislature created a disparity of treatment between similar classes of individuals. The court stated that the true distinction was between occupational diseases and work-related injuries. Having established this distinction on a reasonable basis, such distinction was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board. The court concluded that the automatic 300-week limitation for death claims for compensation provided for in the Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Act did not violate either due process or equal protection.
