Township Supervisors of Adams Township v. West


Nos. 2374 C.D. 1982, 1061 C.D. 1983, 1072 C.D. 1983


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


79 Pa. Commw. 254; 469 A.2d 701; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2212


October 3, 1983, Argued  
December 29, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Butler County in the case of James A. West v. Township Supervisors of Adams Township, Stanley Wilhelm and Clara Wilhelm, Wayne Hindman and Pat Hindman and Thomas Lower and Shirley Lower, A.D. No. 80-726, Book 119, Page 61.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township supervisors and appellee landowner both sought review of orders of the Court of Common Pleas, Butler County (Pennsylvania), which reversed a decision of appellants denying a request for a curative amendment made by appellee. The trial court found the zoning ordinance unconstitutional due to its failure to provide for mobile home parks and ordered appellants to approve appellee's original plan.


OVERVIEW: Appellee landowner submitted a request for a curative amendment to a township zoning ordinance which had no provision for mobile home parks in any of the various zoning districts and sought permission to implement a plan for a mobile home park. Appellant township supervisors denied the request for a curative amendment. Appellee submitted a revised plan to the trial court, and the trial court declared appellants' ordinance unconstitutional for its exclusion of mobile home parks and ordered appellant to approve appellee's original plan. Appellants sought review of the finding of unconstitutionality, and appellee sought review of the trial court's failure to specifically approve his amended plan. The court vacated the orders because the trial court erred in its reliance on a mere showing of total prohibition of mobile home parks to overcome the presumption of the ordinance's validity. The court remanded for the trial court to permit appellee an opportunity to prove an exclusionary result and then determine whether appellant could meet its burden to justify any exclusion. The court found the record insufficient to make the determination.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's orders and remanded for the trial court to analyze whether appellee landowner presented sufficient evidence to show an exclusionary result by appellant township supervisors in their zoning ordinance, because there was insufficient evidence in the record for the court to make the determination. The court found that the burden shifted to appellants to justify the exclusion once appellants met their burden.

Steck v. Commonwealth, Unemployment Compensation Bd. of Review


No. 1278 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


78 Pa. Commw. 514; 467 A.2d 1378; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2143


October 3, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
November 25, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in case of In Re: Claim of Diane M. Steck, No. B-204134.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant challenged an order of respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which denied her benefits on the grounds that she voluntarily terminated her employment.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimant quit her job in order to move with her family when her husband was advised by his physician to move to a warmer and drier climate for health reasons. Respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review argued that claimant's voluntary termination of her employment was without cause of a necessitous and compelling nature. The court held, that under 43 P.S. § 802(b), claimant's obligation to join her spouse could constitute a necessitous and compelling reason to leave her employment. The court held that claimant's husband's move was not a personal whim, but was taken at his doctor's direction, and that there was no move that the husband could have undertaken would have permitted claimant to retain her employment and still be with her family. Therefore, the court reversed because claimant established that her actions were reasonable and in good faith.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review denying petitioner claimant's benefits because claimant's voluntary termination of her job to move with her family, upon her husband's physician's advice, was for cause of a necessitous and compelling nature.

Leonard v. Thornburgh


No. 1724 C.D. 1983


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


78 Pa. Commw. 216; 467 A.2d 104; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2090


September 13, 1983, Argued  
November 4, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in the case of Thomas A. Leonard and Kathleen Leonard and Graveley Roofing Corporation v. Richard L. Thornburgh, Governor, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and James L. Scheiner, Secretary of Revenue, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and William J. Green, Mayor, City of Philadelphia, and Joseph W. Brown, Director of Finance, City of Philadelphia, and Eugene L. Cliett, Jr., Revenue Commissioner, City of Philadelphia.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections partially sustained and partially denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, governor and secretary of revenue, filed preliminary objections to the complaint of petitioners, roofing corporation and certain other individuals, contending that both respondents were not proper parties to the petitioners' action challenging the constitutionality of a state taxing statute.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, governor and secretary of revenue, filed preliminary objections to petitioners', roofing corporation and certain other individuals, complaint which challenged the constitutionality of a taxing statute. Respondents contended that they were not proper parties to the petitioners' action. The court granted respondent governor's objection and held that as the chief executive officer under the authority of the Pa. Const. art. IV, § 2, his interest in faithfully executing the tax laws of the commonwealth was adequately represented by respondent secretary of revenue, and that therefore, respondent governor was not a necessary party to the action. The court held that respondent secretary of revenue was a necessary party and denied his objection. The court also held that it could not have resolved the issue of irreparable harm to petitioners under a constitutional challenge to the nonresident cap because it was not a preliminary matter under Pa. R. Civ. P. 1017.


OUTCOME: The court granted respondent governor's objection to the complaint of petitioners, roofing corporation and certain other individuals, and held that he was not a necessary party for a just adjudication of the action because as the chief executive, his interest in faithfully executing the tax laws of the commonwealth was adequately protected by respondent secretary of revenue, whose objection was overruled.

In re Revocation of Rest. Liquor License No. R-12122


No. 2651 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


78 Pa. Commw. 159; 467 A.2d 85; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2081


September 14, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
November 1, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County in case of Arthur A. Banks v. Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board, No. 360 M.D. 1982.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a decision of the liquor control board that revoked appellant's restaurant liquor license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged an order that affirmed a decision of the liquor control board to revoke his restaurant liquor license. The revocation of appellant's liquor license was based on permitting beer to be furnished or given to minors, permitting the use of a controlled substance on the premises, and selling liquor for consumption off the licensed premises in violation of section 406 of the Liquor Code, 47 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4-406. Appellant argued that if the other sufficient cause standard was constitutional, then a single instance of permitting the use of a controlled substance on the premises could not provide the basis for a license revocation. The revocation was not grounded solely on the basis of the controlled substance charge. The revocation, instead, was supported by the cumulative effect of the three violations. The court concluded that the finding that the use of a controlled substance was permitted on the licensed premises, particularly when considered together with the other violations, supported the instant revocation.


OUTCOME: The decision of the liquor control board that revoked appellant's restaurant liquor license was affirmed because the cumulative violations of the law by appellant's establishment supported the revocation.

Mahoney Area School Dist. v. Gutsie


No. 96 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


78 Pa. Commw. 95; 466 A.2d 1137; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2068


September 12, 1983, Argued  
October 26, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Schuylkill County in case of Peter Gutsie and George M. Walker v. Mahanoy Area School District, Florence Ball, Mahanoy City Tax Collector, Rosemary Gilmore, Mahanoy Township Tax Collector, George Smulligan, Ryan Township Tax Collector, Jack Rice, Rush Township Tax Collector, William Halupa, Gilberton Borough Tax Collector, and Shirley Morgans, Delano Township Tax Collector, No. S-1364 November Term, 1975.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district and various tax collectors sought review of the order from the Court of Common Pleas of Schuylkill County (Pennsylvania) that denied its petition to reopen a default judgment in favor of appellee taxpayers in their class action seeking to have an occupational tax levy declared unconstitutional pursuant to The Local Tax Enabling Act, 53 P.S. §§ 6901-6924, 1965 Pa. Laws 1257.


OVERVIEW: Appellee taxpayers filed a class action against appellant school district and various tax collectors in 1975 seeking a judgment that an occupational tax levied by appellants was unconstitutional under The Local Tax Enabling Act, 53 P.S. §§ 6901-6924, 1965 Pa. Laws 1257. Appellants were granted leave to answer by the trial court, and had requested continuances in order to hire an attorney. When the complaint had remained unanswered in 1979, the trial court entered default judgment. Appellants filed a motion to reopen the case that was denied by the trial court. Appellants then sought review, contending that the trial court had lacked jurisdiction and had abused its discretion in refusing to reopen the case. The court affirmed and held that a petition to open a default judgment can prevail if the following three factors coalesce: a) the petition is promptly filed; b) a meritorious defense can be shown; and c) there is a reasonable excuse for failure to file an answer. The court found no abuse of discretion by the trial court because appellant had failed to provide a reasonable excuse for its failure to answer for such an extended period of time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of appellant school district and various tax collectors' motion to reopen the default judgment because appellant had not demonstrated a reasonable excuse for failing to file an answer despite being aware of its obligation to answer, allowing months to pass before retaining a lawyer, and had asked for several extensions.

St. Christopher's Hospital for Children, Div. of United Hospitals, Inc. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Public Welfare


No. 2871 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


78 Pa. Commw. 113; 466 A.2d 1134; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2070


April 6, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
October 26, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania Department of Public Welfare in case of Appeal of St. Christopher's Hospital for Children, Re: Dwight Blunt and Carol Jackson, No. 1297 184 TC.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner hospital appealed an order from respondent Department of Public Welfare (Pennsylvania) dismissing, on the basis of untimeliness, the administrative appeal taken by petitioner on behalf of a minor patient who was determined to be ineligible for medical assistance.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought review of an order of respondent, the department of public welfare, dismissing the administrative appeal filed by petitioner hospital on behalf of a minor patient who was found to be ineligible for medical assistance. The appeal was dismissed based on untimeliness. Petitioner challenged respondent's action on due process grounds, arguing that respondent unconstitutionally denied it a hearing on the issue of whether its administrative appeal was timely filed. The court reversed the decision and remanded the case. The court held that an applicant for public benefits could not be determined to be ineligible without adequate notice of the reason for rejection and the opportunity to be heard and to defend in an orderly proceeding adapted to the nature of the case. The court found that where a decision on the timeliness of an appeal turned on questions of fact, the claimant had to be afforded an evidentiary hearing. Therefore, the case was remanded in order to afford petitioner an opportunity to inspect relevant agency records and present evidence in support of its claim that the appeal was timely filed.


OUTCOME: The order of respondent department of public welfare dismissing the administrative appeal of petitioner hospital was reversed because petitioner was entitled to an evidentiary hearing on the timeliness issue. The case was remanded.

Guess v. Workmen's Compensation Appeal Bd. (Link Belt/FMC Corp.)


No. 279 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


77 Pa. Commw. 319; 466 A.2d 1098; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2050


April 4, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
October 21, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in the case of Sojourner Guess v. Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board and Link Belt, F.M.C. Corp., No. 5136 March Term, 1977.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant employee sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the decision of respondent workmen's compensation appeal board sustaining the referee's dismissal of claimant's petition for compensation for silicosis filed under the Pennsylvania Occupational Disease Act, 77 P.S. §§ 1201-1603.


OVERVIEW: Claimant employee sought disability compensation benefits for permanent partial disability from silicosis under the Pennsylvania Occupational Disease Act (Act), 77 P.S. §§ 1201-1603. Respondent workmen's compensation appeal board dismissed claimant's petition for failure to prove that he was totally disabled from silicosis as required by section 301(e) of the Act, 77 P.S. § 1401(e). The trial court affirmed expressly rejecting claimant's constitutional challenges to § 1401(e). On appeal, the court found that while § 1401(e) denied claimant compensation for partial, but not total disability due to his silicosis, and barred a common law negligence action against his employer, there was no deprivation of due process. By accepting the legislature's intent to bring all silicosis sufferers under the Act, claimant agreed to look solely to the Act for compensation. Claimant's equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV were not violated because the legislature's desire to limit the impact on the industrial economy was a legitimate objective, which was reasonably related to the Act's classification of partial silicosis as not being compensable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order that affirmed respondent workmen's compensation appeal board's decision sustaining the referee's dismissal of claimant employee's petition for compensation for permanent partial disability from silicosis was affirmed. The court held that the Pennsylvania Occupational Disease Act provisions that limited recovery to total disability did not violate claimant's constitutional rights.

American Trucking Assos. v. Bloom


No. 315 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


77 Pa. Commw. 575; 466 A.2d 755; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2027


September 19, 1983, Heard  
October 17, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania in the case of American Trucking Associations, Inc., and Old Dominion Freight Line, Inc., and Anderson Trucking Service, Inc., individually and on behalf of a class of interstate motor carriers v. Robert K. Bloom, Secretary of the Department of Revenue of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and LeRoy S. Zimmerman, Attorney General of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and Daniel F. Dunn, Commissioner of the State Police of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, challenging the constitutionality of Section 2101 of the Vehicle Code, and requesting that enforcement of the same be enjoined.



DISPOSITION: Statutory provision held unconstitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner trucking association and petitioner foreign motor carriers filed an original action challenging the constitutionality of § 2102(b) of the Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2102(b), which required motor vehicles operating in Pennsylvania to obtain an identification marker upon payment of a fee. Petitioners also sought the refund of all fees.


OVERVIEW: In an original action, petitioner trucking association and petitioner foreign motor carriers challenged the constitutionality of § 2102(b) of the Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2102(b), which required that vehicles operating in Pennsylvania bear an identification marker upon payment of a fee. Petitioners also requested a refund of the fees paid. Petitioners argued that the statute was unconstitutional under the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, because it facially discriminated against foreign-registered vehicles and exempted Pennsylvania registered vehicles from the marker decal fees. The court reviewed the legislative history of the statute and concluded that the statute was intended to exclusively tax foreign-registered vehicles. As the statute facially discriminated in favor of local interests and against foreign-registered vehicles engaging in interstate commerce, it violated the commerce clause's prohibition against interstate commerce. The court therefore declared that the statute was unconstitutional and ordered the refund of fees paid.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the statute requiring motor vehicles operating in Pennsylvania to obtain an identification marker upon payment of a fee violated the commerce clause and was unconstitutional because the statute facially discriminated against foreign-registered vehicles engaged in interstate commerce and exempted local vehicles. The court ordered the refund of fees paid.

Ramsey v. Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 782 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


77 Pa. Commw. 456; 466 A.2d 267; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2035


March 3, 1983, Argued  
October 13, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in the case of Harold J. Ramsey v. Zoning Hearing Board of the Borough of Dormont v. The Borough of Dormont, No. SA 1364 of 1981.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant zoning hearing board sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), reversing appellant's denial of a use conversion permit requested by appellee property owner.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, the owner of a single-family house in a commercial district, sought to convert the property to a conforming commercial use. The application was denied by appellant zoning hearing board on the basis that it was prohibited by Borough of Dormont, Pa., Zoning Ordinance § 504.2. Appellee challenged the denial, and the trial court reversed the denial. Appellant sought review of the order reversing the denial, and the court affirmed. The court noted that within the applicable section of the zoning ordinance, Borough of Dormont, Pa., Zoning Ordinance § 102.2, appellee's building was no longer a dwelling. In addition, the section relied upon by appellant board in denying appellee's application applied only to occupied houses. Because appellee's house was unoccupied, it was no longer a dwelling. Therefore, appellee was entitled to receive a use conversion permit.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court reversing the denial of a use conversion permit requested by appellee property owner was affirmed because appellee's building was not occupied and, thus, was not a dwelling within the applicable zoning ordinance definitions. Therefore, the provisions relied upon in denying the application were inapplicable.

E. Pa. Psychiatric Inst. v. Russell


No. 2350 C.D. 1981, No. 2351 C.D. 1981, No. 2352 C.D. 1981, No. 2353 C.D. 1981, No. 2354 C.D. 1981, No. 2355 C.D. 1981, No. 2356 C.D. 1981, No. 2357 C.D. 1981, No. 2358 C.D. 1981, No. 2359 C.D. 1981, No. 2360 C.D. 1981, No. 2361 C.D. 1981, No. 2362 C.D. 1981, No. 2363 C.D. 1981, No. 2364 C.D. 1981, No. 2365 C.D. 1981, No. 2366 C.D. 1981, No. 2367 C.D. 1981, No. 2436 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


77 Pa. Commw. 390; 465 A.2d 1313; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1995


February 2, 1983, Argued  
October 3, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the State Civil Service Commission in cases of Appeal of Walter N. Baker, No. 3310; Appeal of Paul Mueller, No. 3312; Appeal of Frederick Newman, No. 3313; Samuel Peacock, Jr., No. 3314; Appeal of Donald Rudin, No. 3316; Appeal of Joanne Antanavage, No. 3317; Appeal of Teofila Artymyshyn, No. 3318; Appeal of Carolyn Dunlap, No. 3319; Appeal of Hadassah Freifelder, No. 3320; Appeal of Roy Joshlin, No. 3322; Appeal of Irma Kostyk, No. 3323; Appeal of Martha Kratky, No. 3324; Appeal of David Levitt, No. 3325; Appeal of Patricial Lewis, No. 3326; Appeal of Alma E. Lloyd, No. 3328; Appeal of Sarah Perry, No. 3329; Appeal of Portia Russell, No. 3330; and Appeal of Dolores Smith, No. 3331, dated September 2, 1981.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Department of Public Welfare, challenged the decision from the Pennsylvania State Civil Service Commission, which sustained in part and overruled in part appellant's furlough of appellees, individual employees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, Department of Public Welfare, entered into a contract assuming complete management of a state-owned facility, and notified appellee employees that they would be furloughed. After the trial court entered an injunction, appellant rescinded the furloughs of some employees. After 50 P.S. § 583.1 was enacted, the injunction was lifted and appellant furloughed appellees. The State Civil Service Commission (Commission) held that some furloughs were improper and granted appellees back pay for the period, but held that appellant properly furloughed the employees of the state-owned facility. On appeal, the court held that the finding that some of the furloughs were improper was supported by substantial evidence, as appellant was required to prove not merely that funding was inadequate, but that a rational relationship existed between the lack of funding and the furloughs undertaken. The court held that appellees' due process rights were not violated as appellant was not required to provide appellees a reason for the furlough on the notice, counsel was allowed to review documents, and the consolidated appeal did not result in confusion. The Commission's order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the Pennsylvania State Civil Service Commission that sustained in part, and overruled in part appellant Department of Public Welfare's furlough of appellees, individual employees. The court held that appellant failed to prove not merely that funding was inadequate, but that a rational relationship existed between the lack of funding and the furloughs of appellees.

Am. Fed'n of State v. Commonwealth


No. 2064 C.D. 1983, No. 2160 C.D. 1983, No. 2133 C.D. 1983


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


77 Pa. Commw. 37; 465 A.2d 62; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1926; 4 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2219


August 17, 1983, Hearing Held  
September 2, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in cases of American Federation of State, County and Municipal Employees, AFL-CIO, by its Trustee Ad Litem, Edward J. Keller v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, The Honorable Richard Thornburgh, Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, State Employees' Retirement Board, Robert L. Cusma, Executive Director of the State Employees' Retirement Board, and R. Budd Dwyer, Treasurer of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Dennis J. Solecki and Lea F. Barbush, as Individuals, on behalf of themselves and all others similarly situated v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, The Honorable Richard Thornburgh, Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, State Employees' Retirement Board, Robert L. Cusma, Executive Director of the State Employees' Retirement Board, and R. Budd Dwyer, Treasurer of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; and Joint Bargaining Committee of the Pennsylvania Social Services Union and Pennsylvania Employment Security Employee's Association, Locals 668 and 675, SEIU, AFL-CIO, by its Trustees Ad Litem, Andrew L. Stern and Harry Beshgetoorian, Pennsylvania Social Services Union, by its Trustee Ad Litem, Andrew L. Stern, Frank Catanese, Individually and on [***2] behalf of others similarly situated, and Lillian Swartz, Individually and on behalf of others similarly situated v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, The Honorable Richard Thornburgh, Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, State Employees' Retirement Board, Robert L. Cusma, Executive Director of the State Employees' Retirement Board and R. Budd Dwyer, Treasurer of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Case consolidated. Preliminary injunction granted. Bond ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, including state government labor unions and individual workers, sought to permanently enjoin the enforcement of 1983 Pa. Laws Act 31, which required most state employees, participants in the State Employees' Retirement System, to contribute an additional one and one-fourth percent of their salary to the State Employees' Retirement Fund.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, a consolidated group of state government employees' labor unions and individual workers, challenged the constitutionality of Act No. 31 of 1983 (Act 31), which required most state employees, participants in the state's retirement system, to contribute an additional one and one-fourth percent of their salary to the State Employees' Retirement Fund (fund). Petitioners contended that Act 31's increase in the employee contribution rates without an increase in benefits constituted an improper treatment of contract rights and that Act 31 violated state law requiring the employer state to insure the actuarial stability of the fund. The court granted petitioners' application to enjoin the state from collecting pension contributions in excess of the five percent basic contribution rate. It held that Act 31 was unconstitutional as to those employees whose rights to retirement benefits had already vested, because the increased contribution rate effectively diminished the benefits received. It was unconstitutional as to those employees whose rights had not yet vested, because it did not contain any new benefit to offset the fiscal disadvantage of the increased contributions.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioners' application to enjoin the state from collecting pension contributions in excess of the five percent basic contribution rate from state workers who were participants in the State Employees' Retirement System and held that the act which provided for the increased contributions was unconstitutional.

County of Allegheny v. Wilcox


Nos. 1457 C.D. 1981 and 1464 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


76 Pa. Commw. 584; 465 A.2d 47; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1911; 37 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 659; 39 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P35,901


March 1, 1983, Argued  
August 29, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted January 23, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Order of the Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission in the case of Evelyn M. Wilcox, Nancy G. Carlisle, Florence M. Corbett, Leora K. Flygar, Georgina G. Franci, Margaret Greenawald, Mitzi R. Holtzman, individually and on behalf of all others similarly situated v. County of Allegheny, Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas, Minor Judiciary Courts of Allegheny County, Docket Nos. E-7036P, E-7149P, E-7160P, E-10447, E-10448, E-10449 and E-10450.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, county and court, challenged the order of the Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission, which found that petitioners had violated § 5(a) of the Pennsylvania Human Relations Act, 43 P.S. § 955(a), and ordered petitioners to pay back pay and immediately increase respondent secretaries pay to that equal to the level received by male night court clerks.


OVERVIEW: Respondents were female district justice secretaries employed by petitioner Allegheny County and working for petitioner Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas. Respondents brought an action against petitioners alleging sex discrimination based on the fact that less skilled, but male, night shift court clerks were paid a larger salary than that paid to respondents. The Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission (Commission) found petitioners guilty of sex discrimination, awarded backpay, and ordered petitioners to increase respondents' pay to equal that of the night court clerks. The court affirmed the Commission's order and found that substantial evidence existed that warranted a finding of sex discrimination, there was no appreciable variation in skill, responsibility or effort between the jobs which justified the difference in pay and the fact that the court clerks worked night shift was not persuasive because other employees were not paid differently for the same position on different shifts including other court personnel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against petitioners, county and court, and the orders to pay backpay and increase respondent secretaries' salary to equal that paid to the male night shift court clerks because the record supported the finding that petitioners had engaged in sex discrimination against respondents.

Commonwealth v. Twentier


Nos. 976 C.D. 1982 and 2481 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


76 Pa. Commw. 537; 464 A.2d 642; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1896


March 1, 1983, Argued  
August 24, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied April 30, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County in the case of Raymond W. Twentier and Elfrieda Twentier, his wife v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, No. 525 of 1979; and from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in the case of Neil Reeb v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Transportation, et al., No. 2530 November Term, 1979.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth sought review of orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County (Pennsylvania) and the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which denied the commonwealth's post-trial motions in two separate but consolidated cases. The commonwealth filed post-trial motions in each case to seek to mold appellee victims' personal injury verdicts to the limits imposed by the Sovereign Immunity Act, 42 P.S. § 8528.


OVERVIEW: The trial courts rendered personal injury verdicts in favor of appellee victims and against the commonwealth in two separate but consolidated cases for appeal. The trial courts denied the commonwealth's post-trial motions that sought to mold the verdicts to the $ 250,000 limit imposed by the Sovereign Immunity Act (Act), 42 P.S. § 8528. The court affirmed the orders of the trial courts. The court held that all retroactive applications of the Act were prohibited. The court stated that a law that was enacted after a case had arisen could be no part of the case. The court also held that the assessment of delay damages, pursuant to Pa. R. Civ. P. 238 was constitutional. The court further stated that there was no reason to set the commonwealth apart from other defendants subject to delay damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the trial courts, which denied the commonwealth's post-trial motions in two separate but consolidated personal injury actions brought by appellee victims. The court stated that retroactive application of a statute that limited damages recoverable from the commonwealth to cases that had arisen before enactment of the law was prohibited.

Heller v. Frankston


No. 460 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


76 Pa. Commw. 294; 464 A.2d 581; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1851


September 16, 1982, Argued  
August 11, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Administrator of the Arbitration Panels for Health Care in case of Carmello Marquez, a minor, by Dionisia Marquez, his guardian v. Hahnemann Medical College and Hospital of Philadelphia et al., No. M76-00009.



DISPOSITION: Order of Administrator vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, attorneys, challenged an order of respondent Arbitration Panels for Health Care, (Pennsylvania), directing petitioners to relinquish certain disputed funds relating to the settlement of a medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed and vacated respondent administrator's order directing petitioners, attorneys, to relinquish certain disputed funds relating to the settlement of a medical malpractice action. The court held that 40 P.S. § 1301.604, which regulated the fees received by plaintiffs' attorneys, was unconstitutional because it constituted an impermissible legislative interference with the responsibilities of the judiciary. The court found that the courts of the commonwealth had been addressing issues of attorney's fees for several hundred years, and it was well within the ambit of the constitutionally discrete power of the judiciary to regulate fees charged by lawyers. The court rejected respondent's argument regarding the similarity of provisions in other statutes, relating to the payment of compensation for unemployment, job-related injuries, and loss or injury due to crime, which contain limitations on the fee to be charged by the claimant's attorney because in each of the enactments, the general assembly created the remedy, which had not previously existed as a common law cause of action, as did medical malpractice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated respondent administrator's order, holding that a section of the Health Care Services Malpractice Act was unconstitutional because it constituted an impermissible legislative interference with the responsibilities of the judiciary, a co-equal branch of government, to regulate lawyer's fees.

 

919 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Lower Dauphin School Dist. v. Kutler


No. 179 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


76 Pa. Commw. 87; 463 A.2d 499; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1823


December 18, 1981, Argued  
August 4, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued September 14, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County in case of William J. Kutler and Willard E. Kidwell, on behalf of themselves and all others similarly situated v. Lower Dauphin School District, No. 3247 S 1977, In Assumpsit.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which found that appellees, retirees and housewives, had no taxable occupation for purposes of the tax levied by appellant on occupations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant school district enacted a resolution imposing a tax on occupations as authorized by 53 P.S. § 6902. Appellees, retirees and housewives, paid the taxes and commenced an action to recover the taxes that they claimed were unlawfully levied. The trial court held that appellees did not have taxable occupations and the court affirmed. It held that since an occupation tax was not an income tax, there must be some connectional link between the income exemption provided in the statute and the occupation tax, and determined the link was that only income producing occupations were taxable. The court also determined that the issue was not whether homemakers or retired persons did something of value for themselves or for others, but whether what they did produced a realizable pecuniary benefit which could be used by them to acquire property or support a family. Finally, the court held that the constitutional issue was without merit and it need not consider whether this was a reasonable classification of persons with occupations since they were not subjects of the tax when neither retired persons nor homemakers had taxable occupations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court that appellees, retirees and housewives, had no taxable occupations because their occupations were not income producing.

Sitarik v. Civil Service Com.


No. 98 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


76 Pa. Commw. 29; 462 A.2d 966; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1811


March 2, 1983, Argued  
July 29, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in case of John P. Sitarik, Jr., Regis R. Ricketts, Gary A. Minor, Richard D. Palmieri and Thomas M. DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officers challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed their petition for writ of certiorari complaining of the denial of their request for a hearing regarding the alleged denial of due process of law and unconstitutionality of the promotional procedures under the Police Civil Service Act, 53 P.S. § 23535.


OVERVIEW: Appellant police officers scored highly on a promotional examination, but were passed over for promotion by the superintendent of police, whose selections were based on the superior qualifications of the candidates based on their previous service and experience. Leonard v. Thornburgh


No. 1724 C.D. 1983


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


75 Pa. Commw. 553; 463 A.2d 77; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1779


July 7, 1983, Heard  
July 19, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in the case of Thomas A. Leonard and Kathleen Leonard and Graveley Roofing Corporation v. Richard L. Thornburgh, Governor, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and James L. Scheiner, Secretary of Revenue, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and William J. Green, Mayor, City of Philadelphia, and Joseph W. Brown, Director of Finance, City of Philadelphia, and Eugene L. Cliett, Jr., Revenue Commissioner, City of Philadelphia.



DISPOSITION: Petition of individual plaintiffs denied. Petition of corporate plaintiff transferred to the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, city residents, requested a preliminary injunction be granted that would restrain respondents, the governor and others, from enforcing the Non-Resident Cap found in 72 P.S. § 7359(b) of the Tax Reform Code of 1971. Petitioners contended that the cap, which limited for non-residents only the amount a city could tax on their income, had no justification for treating residents differently.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, city residents, wanted the Non-Resident Cap found in 72 P.S. § 7359(b) of the Tax Reform Code of 1971 declared unconstitutional. The cap limited the tax rate that the city could impose on the salaries, wages, commissions and compensation received by non-residents, but set no similar limit on the tax rate applied against compensation earned by city residents. Petitioners sought a preliminary injunction to enjoin the city from enforcing the amendments. The court regrettably denied the application for preliminary injunction because, although the court found the cap unquantifiable and unrealistic, the greater injury would result by the grant of an injunction. The court reasoned that if it granted the injunction, the effect would have devastated the budget of the city. Petitioners did not establish that the greater injury would result by the denial of the injunction and the court, therefore, would not grant a preliminary injunction.


OUTCOME: The court denied the request for a preliminary injunction of petitioners, city residents. The court found that petitioners had not satisfied their burden of showing that the greater injury would result by the denial of the injunction. Although the court agreed that the non-resident cap on taxes imposed on non-residents was unfair to residents, it would be too disruptive to the city's budget to enjoin enforcement.

Wyatt v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Public Welfare


No. 1353 C.D. 1979


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


75 Pa. Commw. 347; 463 A.2d 64; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1755


September 15, 1981, Argued  
July 5, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued September 14, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue in the case of In Re: Gordon and Teresa Wyatt, Docket No. M-3207.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant appealed from the order of the Board of Finance and Review (Pennsylvania), which denied her petition for refund of monies paid to respondent Department of Public Welfare as reimbursement for public assistance garnered pending receipt of retroactive, lump-sum social security disability insurance benefits payable to petitioner's husband, now deceased.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Department of Public Welfare provided public assistance to petitioner claimant and her family pending receipt of the husband's social security disability insurance benefits. Upon receipt of the benefits, at respondent's caseworker's instructions, petitioner repaid respondent. Petitioner later filed for a refund with the Board of Finance and Revenue (board) and appealed the board's denial to the court. The court reversed the board's decision and entered a judgment in petitioner's favor. The court determined that the five-year limitation period under 72 P.S. § 503(a) applied to petitioner's claim pursuant to a two-part test. Petitioner reimbursed the commonwealth pursuant to § 207 of the Social Security Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 407, which prohibited states from using legal process to obtain public assistance reimbursement from a recipient's social security benefits. The court found that, although respondent's collection method did not constitute legal process, respondent's caseworker misinformed petitioner and affirmatively misled her to believe she had a legal duty to make repayment from the protected benefits. Therefore, the reimbursement was not obtained by fair means.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Board of Finance and Review and ordered that petitioner claimant be refunded the money she paid to respondent Department of Public Welfare. The court held that respondent's collection method did not constitute legal process, which was a prohibited method for obtaining reimbursement from social security benefits; however, repayment was not made by fair means as its caseworker affirmatively misled petitioner.

Commonwealth, Dep't of Transp., Bureau of Traffic Safety v. Slater


No. 1901 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


75 Pa. Commw. 310; 462 A.2d 870; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1751


May 11, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
June 30, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County in the case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Transportation, Bureau of Traffic Safety v. Glenn E. Slater, No. 80-7728.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of transportation sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County (Pennsylvania), which stated that its original order that gave appellee diabetic driver's license back to him should have been reversed. The appeal was treated as an appeal from the decision that restored the license. Appellant contended that, under the Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1504, 1509, appellee was not qualified.


OVERVIEW: Appellant department of transportation revoked the school bus driver's license of appellee diabetic driver. Appellant cited the Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1504, 1509, which required that school bus drivers had to be physically qualified to obtain a license. Specifically, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1517(b) required no medical history of diabetes. The trial court reversed appellant's decision. On further appeal, the court reversed the order and reinstated the revocation of the license. The court found that appellee was not deprived of a fundamental right even though he used the license to drive and for his livelihood. The license was a privilege, not a right. Appellee presented no evidence to refute the underlying assumption of § 1517(b). Absent any refutation, the court did not find appellant's decision and its method of ensuring safe school bus drivers were irrational. The court did not deviate from traditional equal protection and due process analysis, even where appellee challenged a statutory presumption. The classification adopted by appellant was not suspect, did not impair fundamental rights, and was rationally related to a legitimate state purpose.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the original order of the trial court, that had allowed appellee diabetic driver to retain his license. The court held that appellant department of transportation's suspension of the license was reinstated because appellee did not rebut the presumption that diabetic drivers were hazardous to the safety of buses. The court used traditional equal protection and due process analyses.

Muhlenberg Township Authority v. Reading


No. 342 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


75 Pa. Commw. 227; 461 A.2d 654; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1739


May 11, 1983, Argued  
June 27, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County in the case of Muhlenberg Township Authority v. City of Reading, Nos. 16 June 1981, A.D., 34 June 1981, J.D. and 132 October 1980, M.L.D.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County (Pennsylvania), which awarded summary judgment to appellee city in a scire facias sur municipal claim, and struck off an assessment lien for sewer improvements by appellant, which had benefited appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant township sought review of a decision, from a scire facias sur municipal claim, which awarded summary judgment to appellee city, and struck off an assessment lien for a sewer improvement, which appellant had filed against appellee. The court reversed and held that city property used for a public purpose, and located within an adjacent township, was not exempt from the lien of an assessment for the benefits of a sewer project constructed by the township's authority. The Pennsylvania Lien Act, 53 P.S. § 7108 provided that all real estate, other than state or federal land, was subject to municipal claims except that municipal and charitable property, if legally nontaxable, was not the subject of municipal claims except for sewer, nuisance and paving claims. The statute made all property subject to municipal claims, and the exemption for public property did not extend to sewer liens; § 7108 left municipal property subject to the fundamental rule of assessability for sewer benefits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision that granted summary judgment against appellant township, in a scire facias sur municipal claim, and that struck off an assessment lien for a sewer improvement, which appellant had filed against appellee city. A plain reading of the Pennsylvania Lien Act left municipal property subjected to the fundamental rule of assessability for sewer benefits; sewer liens were not exempted.

Osser v. Philadelphia


No. 14 T.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


75 Pa. Commw. 145; 461 A.2d 639; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1722


April 7, 1983, Argued  
June 20, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in the case of Maurice Osser v. City of Philadelpha, No. 2352 August Term, 1976.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which refused to direct payment by respondent city of his accrued pension benefits.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee resigned after he was convicted in federal court for mail fraud, conspiracy, and endeavoring to obstruct criminal investigation in violation of 18 U.S.C.S. §§ 1341, 1342, 371, and 1510. Subsequent to his conviction and resignation, appellant filed a claim with the Board of Pensions and Retirement of respondent city which was denied. Appellant then filed a complaint in the trial court, which denied relief pursuant to, inter alia, the Philadelphia Retirement System Ordinance § 217. On review, the court reversed. The court agreed with appellant that, notwithstanding the ordinance, the terms of his pension contract were fixed prior to its enactment, and thus, the forfeiture provisions could not be applied to him. The court held that pensions were deferred compensation for services rendered in the past and could not, under law, be adversely affected by unilateral governmental changes after appellant's initial membership in the system.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and remanded the case with directions to remand to respondent city's Board of Pensions and Retirement for the computation of benefits. The court found that pensions for public employees, including appellant employee, were deferred compensation for services rendered and the rights of an employee could not be adversely affected by unilateral governmental changes after initial membership in the system.

Hess v. Montgomery County Bd. of Assessment Appeals


No. 704 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


75 Pa. Commw. 69; 461 A.2d 333; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1704


April 5, 1983, Argued  
June 13, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County in case of Jane Strayer Hess and Lawrence Eugene Hess, Jr. v. Montgomery County Board of Assessment Appeals, No. 79-14568.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant land owners sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which rejected appellants' constitutional challenge to the provisions of the Pennsylvania Farmland and Forest Land Assessment Act of 1974, 72 P.S. §§ 55490.1 - 5490.13, which placed a ten acre minimum area requirement on the availability of preferential tax treatment for "forest reserves."


OVERVIEW: Appellant land owners owned land that included six acres of forest land. Appellants applied for a preferential property tax assessment for their forest land pursuant to the Pennsylvania Farmland and Forest Land Assessment Act of 1974, 72 P.S. §§ 55490.1 - 5490.13. The Board of Assessment Appeals determined that appellants' were not entitled to preferential tax assessments under the Act. Appellants sought review of the trial court's decision, which affirmed the board. Appellants argued that, although Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 2(b)(i) did authorize special tax treatment for forest reserves, the uniformity clause remained applicable and required that all forest land be treated alike without regard to acreage. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that as a result of the adoption of Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 2(b)(i), the general assembly was empowered to treat "forest reserves", "agriculture reserves" and "land actively devoted to agricultural use" as separate classes of real estate entitled to special provision for taxation which were not subject to the uniformity clause. Thus, appellants' land was not entitled to preferential tax assessments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that appellant land owners were not entitled to preferential tax assessment of their forest land because appellants failed to meet their heavy burden of demonstrating that the Pennsylvania Farmland and Forest Land Assessment Act of 1974 clearly and plainly violated the Pennsylvania Constitution.

In re Appeal from Settlement & Audit of Auditors of Buckingham Township


No. 1204 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


74 Pa. Commw. 614; 460 A.2d 904; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1685


April 5, 1983, Argued  
June 6, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County in the case of In Re: Appeal from Settlement and Audit of the Auditors of Buckingham Township, Bucks County, Pennsylvania, of the Annual Audit and Financial Report for the year 1978, No. 79-6418-09-6.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town supervisors sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which subjected appellants to a surcharge for monies unlawfully paid from town funds.


OVERVIEW: Appellant town supervisors sought review of the trial court's order, which subjected appellants to a surcharge for monies unlawfully paid out of town funds. Appellants argued that the trial court erred in not quashing the taxpayers' appeal, that 53 P.S. § 65725 impliedly gave the township power to pay the expenses, that the surcharge was not proper under 46 P.S. 148(ii)(C), that their conduct was authorized by 53 P.S. § 10209.1, and that the surcharge was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the recognizance complied with the township's ordinances, and quashing was not warranted. The court held that lobbying in any sense could not be considered a necessarily implied power under 53 P.S. § 65725. The court held that there was doubt that appellants' expenditures were covered by 46 P.S. 148(ii)(C), and must be resolved against appellants. Also, the court held that appellants did not offer sufficient evidence to prove that the expenses incurred were "necessary and reasonable." Finally, the court held that the action was not unconstitutional because it did not abridge the rights of appellants to speak their views on legislation or to seek redress of grievances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which subjected appellant town supervisors' to a surcharge for monies unlawfully paid out of town funds, because the power to pay any lobbying expenses was not an impliedly necessarily power. The court also held that appellants' conduct was not authorized by statute. Finally, the court held that the surcharge was proper and constitutional.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of an order of the State Civil Service Commission (Pennsylvania), which ordered respondent governmental employer to reinstate petitioner without back pay.


OVERVIEW: Respondent governmental employer dismissed petitioner employee for failing to fully disclose his police record on his civil service application. Auerbach v. Council Rock School Dist.


No. 639 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


74 Pa. Commw. 507; 459 A.2d 1376; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1663


April 4, 1983, Argued  
May 27, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County in the case of Roger Auerbach and Joan Auerbach, parents and natural guardians of Peter Buttschardt, a minor v. Council Rock School District and John Ciociola, Addl. Deft., No. 81-03339-12-1.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents of injured student, sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee school district's motion for summary judgment in the underlying tort claim, pursuant to the Political Subdivision Tort Claims Act, 53 P.S. § 5311.101 (repealed 1980). Appellants argued that it was unconstitutional to hold appellee immune under the act.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, parents of injured student, argued that appellee school district failed to take adequate measures to protect appellants' child's safety and failed to supervise the other students, one of whom allegedly injured appellant's child. The trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment, citing the Political Subdivision Tort Claims Act, Act of November 26, 1978, 53 P.S. § 5311.101 (repealed 1980), and holding that appellee was immune. Appellants argued that the act was unconstitutional as applied to the facts and circumstances of their claim and in light of Pa. Const. art. III, § 14, which provided for the maintenance and support of a thorough and efficient system of public education to serve the needs of the commonwealth. The court rejected appellants' arguments and held that school districts were immune under the act. The court found that Pa. Const. art. III, § 14 was never intended to mean that tort liability should be imposed upon a school district when students were injured in the course of the school day, even if there was negligence on the part of the school officials. The court therefore affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellee school district in appellants parents of injured student's tort claim. The court found that the lower court was correct in determining that school districts were immune to such suits under the Political Subdivision Tort Claims Act.

Gulf & Western Corp. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Labor & Industry, etc.


No. 1238 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


74 Pa. Commw. 493; 459 A.2d 1369; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1659


March 1, 1983, Argued  
May 26, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Employer Accounts Review Board in the case of Gulf & Western Corporation v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Labor and Industry, Office of Employment Security, Employer Accounts Review Board, Account No. 99-22322.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation sought review of an order of respondent Employer Accounts Review Board of the Department of Labor and Industry (Pennsylvania), which upheld a revised contribution rate assigned to petitioner's account pursuant to the Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Law, 43 P.S. §§ 751-914.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner corporation had its unemployment compensation debit reserve balance adjusted to zero, pursuant to 43 P.S. § 782(c), and its contribution rate was set at the four percent maximum for the years 1978, 1979, and 1980, pursuant to 43 P.S. § 781.1(f). The legislature enacted amendments raising the maximum contribution rate, retroactively effective to January 1, 1980. Petitioner's contribution rate for 1980 was then revised upward to 5.65 percent. Petitioner argued that because the amendment provided a higher contribution rate, its 1980 contribution rate should remain at four percent. On appeal the court held that 43 P.S. § 781.1(f.1) governed and authorized the recalculation of the 1980 contribution rate. Petitioner also argued that respondent Employer Accounts Review Board of the Department of Labor and Industry was estopped from altering the contribution rate because respondent accepted and approved petitioner's application to adjust its reserve balance to zero. The court affirmed the order and held that there was no contractual relationship, and even if there had been, petitioner's election was subject to the reservation in 43 P.S. § 881.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent employer accounts review board. Petitioner corporation's election to have its unemployment compensation debit reserve adjusted to zero was subject to the legislature's power to amend, and there had been no violation of petitioner's constitutional rights.

Shoenhair v. Commonwealth, Dep't of State, Bureau of Professional & Occupational Affairs


No. 204 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


74 Pa. Commw. 217; 459 A.2d 877; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1601


February 3, 1983, Argued  
May 9, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Department of State, Bureau of Professional and Occupational Affairs, the State Board of Nurse Examiners in the case of In the Matter of the Suspension or Revocation of a License to Practice Professional Nursing, No. RN-171360-L, issued August 7, 1969, to Dona Jean Shoenhair, R.N., dated January 22, 1982.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner nurse appealed an order from respondent Pennsylvania Board of Nurse Examiners, which revoked her Pennsylvania nursing license because her license in a sister state was revoked, as required by The Professional Nursing Law, 63 P.S. § 224(6).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner nurse was found guilty of unprofessional conduct in Florida and her license to practice nursing in Florida was revoked. She did not challenge the Florida revocation and began working in Pennsylvania. Respondent state board of nurse examiners revoked petitioner's Pennsylvania license on the basis of the Florida revocation, pursuant to The Professional Nursing Law, 63 P.S. § 224(6). Respondent held that it could not overlook petitioner's misconduct in Florida, regardless that petitioner was currently conducting herself in a professional and responsible manner. Respondent reasoned that nursing documentation should always be consistent, accurate, and complete. On appeal, petitioner contended that the Pennsylvania revocation was violative of her due process rights because it was dependent on an allegedly faulty Florida proceeding. The court held that petitioner had waived her rights to a Florida hearing by not challenging the revocation and could not collaterally attack that waiver in a Pennsylvania court. The court was bound by the presumption that the Florida revocation was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent state board of nurse examiners, which revoked the nursing license of petitioner nurse, because the court could not say as a matter of law that respondent abused its discretion where it was proven that petitioner's nursing license was revoked in a sister state.

Hawrylak v. Commonwealth, Unemployment Compensation Bd. of Review


Nos. 3027 C.D. 1980, 3028 C.D. 1980, 150 C.D. 1981, 1129 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


74 Pa. Commw. 223; 459 A.2d 883; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1602


November 15, 1982, Argued  
May 9, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in cases of In re: Claim of Louis J. Hawrylak, No. B-189490; Claim of Alvin C. Moyer, No. B-189403; Claim of Nick Chubarov, No. B-190887, and Claim of Harry J. Logue, No. B-204618.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania) orders affirming referees' decisions upholding the Office of Employment Security's deduction of petitioners' social security old age payments and pensions from their unemployment weekly benefit rates pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 804(d)(iii).


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were either retired or were laid off by their respective employers due to lack of work. Petitioners applied for unemployment compensation benefits. Although petitioners were found eligible for unemployment benefits, under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 804(d)(iii) each petitioner's weekly benefit rate was reduced by the amount of social security and private pension payments received. The Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Board) affirmed the referees' decisions upholding the reduction of petitioners' weekly benefits. Petitioners challenged these orders on appeal. On appeal, petitioners challenged the constitutionality of 26 U.S.C.S. § 3304(a)(15). The court dismissed petitioners' appeal without addressing the merits. The issued raised on appeal by some petitioners regarding § 3304(a)(15) was not properly before the court because petitioners did not raise the constitutionality of any statutes before the board. Some petitioners' raised the issue of the constitutionality of the statutes before the referee, but only raised the constitutionality of § 3304(a)(15) on appeal. However, the Board's decision was only issued pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 804(d)(iii).


OUTCOME: The court dismissed petitioners' appeal without addressing the merits and the court affirmed the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review's orders because the constitutionality contentions of petitioners were not properly before the court.

Oppenheim v. Commonwealth, Dep't of State, etc.


No. 3080 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


74 Pa. Commw. 200; 459 A.2d 1308; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1594


April 6, 1983, Argued  
May 6, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Dental Council and Examining Board in the case of in the Matter of the Suspension or Revocation of Dental License No. DS-20111-L, issued July 14, 1977 to Kenneth R. Oppenheim, D.D.S. and in the Matter of the Suspension or Revocation of Dental License No. DS-19309-L, issued October 28, 1975 to Steven M. Sloane, D.D.S., File No. 79-DE-1615, dated November 12, 1981.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner dentists challenged the orders of respondent State Dental Council and Examining Board which suspended their licenses for 90 days.


OVERVIEW: Respondent State Dental Council and Examining Board suspended the licenses of petitioner dentists after finding that petitioners had allowed unlicensed dental hygienists to perform oral prophylaxis in violation of §§ 3(I) and 10 of the Dental Law (Act), 63 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 122(I) and 129. Petitioners challenged that decision. On appeal, the court affirmed. Substantial evidence supported respondent's findings that petitioners' dental assistants were performing unsupervised oral prophylaxis on a regular basis. The court rejected petitioners' argument that the provisions used to suspend their licenses were unconstitutionally vague. Petitioners had adequate notice of the conduct that would render them liable to penalties under the Act. The court also rejected petitioners' argument that respondent violated their due process rights to a fair and impartial tribunal by commingling prosecutorial and adjudicative functions. The court refused to reverse respondent's order merely because certain doctors made the initial decision to proceed to final hearing and then sat as members of the formal hearing tribunal. Also, there was no evidence to suggest that respondent's members were biased.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent's decision to suspend petitioner dentists' licenses. Substantial evidence showed that petitioners had allowed unlicensed dental assistants to perform oral prophylaxis in violation of the applicable law. The applicable law was not void for vagueness. There was no evidence that respondent commingled prosecutorial and adjudicative functions, or that respondent's members were biased against petitioners.

In re Return of the Mercer County Tax Claim Bureau of the Tax Sale Held September 14


No. 1351 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


74 Pa. Commw. 39; 458 A.2d 1074; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1573


March 3, 1983, Argued  
May 3, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County in case of In Re: Return of the Mercer County Tax Claim Bureau of the Tax Sale held September 14, 1981, continued to September 21, 1981 and September 28, 1981. Appeal of Quality Home Improvement Company, No. 1340 C.D. 1980.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of the County of Mercer (Pennsylvania), which confirmed a sale conducted by the county Tax Claim Bureau of appellant's properties for delinquent real estate taxes pursuant to the Real Estate Tax Sale Law, 72 P.S. § 5860.101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation was the owner of two properties, which were sold pursuant to the Real Estate Tax Sale Law, 72 P.S. § 5860.101 et seq. Prior to the sale, appellant had received notice that the properties would be sold because of delinquent real estate taxes: appellant sent a check to the Tax Claim Bureau (bureau), which returned the check, indicating that a higher amount of taxes were owed. The trial court confirmed the sale and the court affirmed on the basis that after an attempted payment of the taxes, appellant failed to do anything further to prevent the sale. The court held that installment payments of the taxes under § 603, 72 P.S. § 5860.603, was not a matter of right, but was at the option of the bureau. Because appellant never requested an installment agreement, its argument that § 603 was unconstitutional on equal protection grounds was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's confirmation of the sale of appellant corporation's properties made pursuant to the Real Estate Tax Sale Law, because the burden to prevent the sale was on appellant.
