Latella v. Unemployment Compensation Bd. of Review


Nos. 3014 C.D. 1980, 3015 C.D. 1980, 3016 C.D. 1980, 3132 C.D. 1980, 3133 C.D. 1980, 3134 C.D. 1980, 3164 C.D. 1980, 103 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


74 Pa. Commw. 14; 459 A.2d 464; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1568


November 16, 1982, Argued  
April 29, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Unemployment Compensation Board in cases of In re: Claims of Catherine Latella, No. B-189407; Antoinette Uliano, No. B-189409; Evelyn B. Drake, No. B-189408; Margaret Capello, B-189991; Thelma Goldian, No. B-190046; Jack Kopf, No. B-190043; Joseph H. Nash, No. B-190708, and Mary Oberholzer, No. B-191329.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part. Deductions of disqualifying retirement income from weekly benefit rates affirmed. Deduction of disqualifying retirement income from total benefit year entitlement under Part E tables reversed and case remanded. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner and similarly situated unemployment claimants sought review from respondent Unemployment Compensation Board (Pennsylvania), which upheld the Office of Employment Security's deduction of social security old age payments from petitioners' unemployment compensation weekly benefit rates in accordance with § 404(d)(iii) of the Unemployment Compensation Law, 43 P.S. § 804(d)(iii).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimants, all of whom were age 62 or over, were laid off by their respective employers due to lack of work. Petitioners filed for unemployment and were found to be eligible for benefits under § 404(d)(iii) of the Unemployment Compensation Law, 43 P.S. § 804(d)(iii). However, the weekly benefit rate was reduced by the amount of social security payments received. Petitioners objected to the reduction. Respondent Unemployment Compensation Board upheld the Office of Employment Security's deduction and the matter was appealed. On review, the court determined that the classification established by the law was rationally related to legitimate governmental purposes. The court upheld respondent's finding requiring the deduction of disqualifying retirement income from the weekly benefit rates. The order was affirmed in that respect. However, the court found that the offsetting of disqualifying wage-replacement income was not provided for under the statute. Therefore, the action by respondent was contrary to law and the decision was reversed and remanded in that respect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent Unemployment Compensation Board's finding which required the deduction of disqualifying retirement income from the weekly benefit rates of petitioner unemployment claimants. But, the order offsetting the disqualifying wage-replacement income was contrary to law where it was not provided for under the Unemployment Compensation Law. That part of the order was reversed and remanded.

 

936 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Widmyer v. Commonwealth


No. 15 T.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


73 Pa. Commw. 581; 458 A.2d 1048; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1561


March 2, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
April 26, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County in case of City of Sharon v. Gerda Widmyer, No. 7 Summary, 1979.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County (Pennsylvania), which fined petitioner and held in a de novo hearing that petitioner violated a local nuisance ordinance in an action initiated by the complaint of petitioner's neighbor who found dog defecation on petitioner's property offensive. Petitioner contended that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to adequately notify her of a violation.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's neighbor complained of offense odors coming from dog defecation on petitioner's property. The neighbor sought civil relief by invoking a local nuisance ordinance. A district justice found petitioner in violation of the ordinance and imposed a fine. Petitioner appealed and the trial court found that she had violated the ordinance in a de novo hearing. Petitioner appealed the decision and contended that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to adequately notify her that the situation could be a violation of the ordinance. The court affirmed the trial court and held that a person of ordinary intelligence would have regarded an offensive aroma which was carried to other locations in the neighborhood as a violation of the ordinance. The ordinance gave petitioner a reasonable opportunity to know that such a condition was prohibited so that she could have acted accordingly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order which fined petitioner and held in a de novo hearing that petitioner violated a local nuisance ordinance by allowing offensive orders emanate from dog defecation on her property because the ordinance gave petitioner a reasonable opportunity to know that such conduct was prohibited and therefore the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

937 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Kleban v. Commonwealth, Unemployment Compensation Bd. of Review


No. 2467 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


73 Pa. Commw. 540; 459 A.2d 53; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1547


March 2, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
April 21, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in case of In Re: Claim of Carole J. Kleban, No. B-170111-B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner ex-employee sought review of an order of respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), that affirmed a referee's decision that she was ineligible for benefits because she left work without a necessitous and compelling cause under the Unemployment Compensation Law § 402(b), 43 P.S. § 802(b). Petitioner had terminated her job to join her husband in Pittsburgh where he had obtained work on a construction project.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner ex-employee had a job but quit it. Her husband was an electrician that had been unemployed. However, he found work in a different city, and petitioner quit her job to join him in that city. Petitioner filed for unemployment compensation. A referee denied her benefits under the Unemployment Compensation Law § 402(b), 43 P.S. § 802(b), and respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review affirmed. Petitioner appealed to the court. The court affirmed. Moving to joining a relocated spouse could provide a necessitous and compelling reason to quit employment thereby entitling one to unemployment compensation. It had to be determined whether or not the relocation was the result of circumstances beyond the husband's control or instead was the product of a purely personal preference. The court relied on respondent's finding that petitioner's husband was regularly transferred to different job sites. The court found that the record showed nothing that contradicted this. The court held that the transient nature of the husband's work prevented it from ruling that petitioner's quitting her job was necessitous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review. The court determined that the referee had found that petitioner ex-employee's husband was regularly transferred to different job sites. The court held that, given the transient character of the work of petitioner husband, it could not say that the basis for petitioner's decision to quit was a necessitous one.

 

938 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Lower Merion


No. 2757 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


73 Pa. Commw. 376; 457 A.2d 1342; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1515


December 15, 1982, Argued  
April 11, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County in the case of Raymond J. Murphy v. Township of Lower Merion, Board of Commissioners of Lower Merion Township Civil Service Commission, G. Andrew McLaughlin, Bruce W. Kauffman, and William F. Davis, III, No. 80-3049.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed appellant's suit against appellees seeking to enjoin appellees from holding a hearing on appellant's demotion in rank.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a police sergeant, responded to a complaint and thereafter discovered that his mace and other gear had been stolen from his police vehicle. The superintendent of police filed a statement of charges against appellant charging him with dereliction of duty, and notified him that he would be demoted. Appellees, the board of commissioners, approved the demotion. Appellant then filed a complaint in equity against appellees in the trial court to enjoin appellees from holding a hearing on his demotion in rank. The trial court dismissed the complaint and appellant sought the court's review. The court held that a court would only exercise its equitable powers when the statutorily prescribed remedy had been exhausted. Here, a statutory remedy clearly existed under the First Class Township Code, 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 55645, which stated that the method of appealing reductions in rank required the person who was reduced in rank to appeal to the county court of common pleas. Therefore, because appellant failed to exhaust his statutory remedies, the trial court properly dismissed his complaint. Accordingly, the order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Order of dismissal affirmed where appellant's equity suit against appellees was improper as appellant had failed to first exhaust the statutory remedies available to him as an individual whose rank had been reduced.

Novak v. Unemployment Compensation Bd. of Review


No. 2072 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


73 Pa. Commw. 148; 457 A.2d 610; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1466


October 7, 1982, Argued  
March 25, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in the case of In Re: Claim of Don W. Novak, No. B-197624.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant appealed from the order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review which denied him benefits under the Unemployment Compensation Law.


OVERVIEW: Claimant was employed until he was laid off due to poor business conditions. Prior to his employment with this particular company, he had served 22 years with the U.S. Marine Corps for which he received a month pension. Claimant applied for unemployment benefits and was notified that he was ineligible for benefits. Claimant contended that by virtue of a 1980 amendment to the Federal Unemployment Tax Act, federal law pre-empted 43 P.S. § 804. This amendment referred to the Multiemployer Pension Plan Amendment Act of 1980. The court held that the Pennsylvania law clearly met the minimum standards as set forth in federal law. Accordingly, it could not be said that state law was in conflict with federal law as to render the doctrine of preemption applicable. The court also dismissed claimant's procedural due process claim. Claimant was afforded a fair hearing and had his benefits reduced according to law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the board of unemployment compensation which denied claimant benefits. On appeal, the court held that the state law which precluded claimant from obtaining unemployment compensation due to his military pension was not preempted by federal law.

Denoncourt v. Commonwealth, State Ethics Com.


No. 2793 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


73 Pa. Commw. 59; 457 A.2d 213; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1449


November 16, 1982, Argued  
March 21, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in the case of Ann Denoncourt, Donald Tinsman, Linda T. Butler and Rudolph E. Butler, Jr. v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, State Ethics Commission.



DISPOSITION: Summary judgment entered in favor of respondent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners school board directors or spouses of directors filed a motion for summary judgment under Pa. R. Civ. P. 1035 in their suit against respondent State Ethics Commission, challenging the constitutionality of 65 P.S. §§ 401-413. Petitioners argued that disclosure of the financial interests of a public official's immediate family, under 65 P.S. § 405, violated the constitutional right of privacy of the family members.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, school board directors and their spouses, challenged the constitutionality of 65 P.S. §§401-413. They argued that 65 P.S. § 405, which required disclosure of the financial interests of a public official's immediate family, violated the constitutional right of privacy of the family members. They also argued that 65 P.S. § 409, which subjected public officials to criminal penalties if such disclosures were not made, violated their due process rights. The court noted that pursuant to 65 P.S. § 401, the act had to be liberally construed in favor of disclosure, that all statutes carried the presumption of constitutionality, and that petitioners had a heavy burden of showing unconstitutionality. The court found that petitioners did not meet their burden of showing the spousal reporting requirements of the act to be an invasion of their privacy rights. The court also found that due process was clearly satisfied as § 409 did not impose absolute or automatic liability. Petitioners' motion for summary judgment was denied.


OUTCOME: Petitioners' motion for summary judgment was denied and summary judgment was entered in favor of respondent because petitioners failed their burden of proving the financial disclosure act unconstitutional.

Long v. Kistler


No. 494 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


72 Pa. Commw. 547; 457 A.2d 591; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1419


December 13, 1982, Argued  
March 14, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in the case of David L. Long, Roger F. Fosbenner, John D. Young, individually and as representative of a class v. Jean E. Kistler, Chairman, State Tax Equalization Board, Upper Perkiomen School District.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections partially sustained and partially overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent school district raised several preliminary objections to a petition for review in the nature of an action in equity, filed by petitioners as representatives of taxpayers in the school district, which contended that the tax levy on their properties was not uniform with the tax placed on the property of other residents of the school district who resided in another county. Petitioners sought an injunction and a rebate of excess taxes.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed a petition for review in the nature of an action in equity for themselves and as representatives of a class of taxpayers in respondent school district, contending that the tax levy on their properties was not uniform with the tax placed on the property of other district residents who resided in another county. Petitioners argued that they had no statutory remedy available to them, and thus sought an injunction and a rebate of excess taxes billed to them. Respondent raised several preliminary objections. The court held it was of the opinion that the petitioners did not have an adequate statutory remedy and that equity was therefore proper. Also, because petitioners had also brought suit in federal court, that court's decision on petitioners' federal claims was res judicata, but not so as to petitioners' state law claims. Laches also did not operate as a valid bar to petitioners' action, because respondent had been aware of petitioners' contentions. As such, the preliminary objection by respondent in the nature of a demurrer raising res judicata was sustained only to petitioners' federal law claims, and all other preliminary objections were overruled.


OUTCOME: In regard to petitioners' action in equity for an injunction and rebate of excess taxes paid on a tax levy that was allegedly non-uniform between school district residents of different counties, the court only sustained the preliminary objection in the nature of a demurrer as to federal law claims as a federal court decision was res judicata on such claims. All other preliminary objections were overruled.

United States Steel Corp. v. Workmen's Comp. Appeal Bd. (mehalovich)


Nos. 1832 C.D. 1980, 1833 C.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


72 Pa. Commw. 481; 457 A.2d 155; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1396


November 15, 1982, Argued  
March 8, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board in the cases of Betty Jane Mehalovich, w/o Michael v. U.S. Steel Corporation and Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, No. A-78560, and Angeline Kuchoric, w/o William v. U.S. Steel Corporation and Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, No. A-78553.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer sought review of an order from respondent, the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Pennsylvania), denying its claim for attorney fees and costs, which were incurred in defending claims filed by respondent employees.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employer challenged an order from respondent, the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board, denying its claim for attorney fees and costs. Petitioner contended that claims filed by respondent employees were filed in bad faith and that, therefore, it was entitled to recover the costs and fees necessary in defending the claims. Petitioner noted that § 440 of the Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Act (Act), 77 P.S. § 996, imposed attorney fees on an employer when it unreasonably contested a claim. Petitioner argued that the same principle should apply when an employee brings a claim in bad faith. The court affirmed the order denying petitioner's claims for costs and fees, finding that § 440 of the Act was not unconstitutional because it was rationally related to a legitimate government interest. The court explained that the Act was intended to benefit employees. Finally, the court explained that it was not authorized to review respondent employees' claims to determine whether they were filed in bad faith.


OUTCOME: The order from respondent, the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board, denying petitioner employer's claim for attorney fees and costs, which were incurred in defending claims filed by respondent employees, was affirmed. The court found that the Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Act was intended to benefit employees, not employers.

In re Friedman


No. 2311 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


72 Pa. Commw. 274; 457 A.2d 983; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1363


January 31, 1983, Argued  
February 23, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Insurance Commissioner of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania in the case of In Re: Albert C. Friedman, Docket No. P80-6-11.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the Order of the Insurance Commissioner of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania in which the Commissioner invoked petitioner's agent's license and ordered him to pay a fine.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was found guilty of conspiracy and interstate transportation of stolen property. Petitioner transferred life insurance policies of his clients from one company to another and converted refund checks to his own use. Respondent also revoked petitioner's agent's license and fined him. One issue on appeal was whether respondent violated his constitutional guarantee against double jeopardy by fining him under the Insurance Department Act of 1921 (Act), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 40, § 279 after the court had already imposed a criminal penalty. The court held the Act empowered respondent to impose a civil penalty of not more than one thousand dollars for each violation upon evidence of conduct which disqualified an agent from initial issuance of a license. Because the language of the Act authorized civil rather than criminal sanctions, the court held that respondent's fine was civil and not criminal. The court rejected petitioner's double jeopardy claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commissioner's decision and held petitioner's double jeopardy claim had no merit because the commissioner's fine was civil and not criminal.

Macon v. Commonwealth Pennsylvania Bd. of Probation & Parole

Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of an order from respondent, the Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, recommitting him as a convicted parole violator for 33 months back time upon his plea of guilty to aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner inmate challenged a decision from respondent, the Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, to recommit him as a convicted parole violator for 33 months back time. OUTCOME: The order recommitting petitioner as a convicted parole violator for 33 months back time upon his plea of guilty to aggravated assault was affirmed because petitioner received a sentence within the presumptive range.

 

945 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Lal v. West Chester Area School Dist.


No. 12 T.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


71 Pa. Commw. 236; 455 A.2d 1240; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1224


November 15, 1982, Argued  
January 18, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Amrit Lal v. West Chester Area School Districts, Tax Claim Bureau, Tax Collector, Thornbury Township and Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and Department of Education.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, school districts, a tax claim bureau, a tax collector, a town, and the Pennsylvania Department of Education, filed preliminary objections to petitioner taxpayer's complaint regarding a school district tax.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner taxpayer challenged the constitutionality of the public school financing system and petitioned the court to dismiss, reduce, or set aside the tax lien against his property after respondent tax collector refused to accept petitioner's late payment of school taxes. The court held that petitioner failed to state a cause of action and that he failed to pursue adequate statutory remedies. The court noted that pursuant to 72 P.S. § 5511.7, petitioner's failure to receive notice of the school tax did not relieve him from the payment of that tax. Additionally, respondent tax collector properly refused to accept petitioner's offer to pay the tax without the penalty imposed under 72 P.S. § 5511.10 because the penalty was added to the tax to constitute the total tax bill. Petitioner's constitutional challenge was to the administration of the property tax and not its constitutionality. Petitioner failed to state a cause of action because he failed to allege any legal injury to any student in respondent school district and failed to allege that students were denied an adequate, basic education.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the preliminary objections of respondents, school districts, a tax claim bureau, a tax collector, a town, and the Pennsylvania Department of Education, to petitioner taxpayer's complaint regarding a school district tax because petitioner failed to state a cause of action. Petitioner owed the tax and penalty, although he did not receive notice of the tax, and he failed to allege a legal injury to any student.

Schoenhut v. Commonwealth, State Real Estate Com.


No. 1635 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


71 Pa. Commw. 230; 455 A.2d 225; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1206


June 11, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
January 17, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Real Estate Commission in case of In the Matter of the Suspension or Revocation of Real Estate Broker's License No. RB-026042-A and RM-026042-A issued to William F. Schoenhut, Jr. and In the Matter of the Suspension or Revocation of Real Estate Broker's License No. RB-028346-A issued to W.F. Schoenhut Corporation, Docket No. 1077, dated June 9, 1981.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner broker appealed to a trial court (Pennsylvania) from a decision and order of respondent state Real Estate Commission revoking his real estate license. After a hearing, petitioner's license was revoked pursuant to the Real Estate Brokers Act of 1929, 63 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 440(a), 441(b), because of his convictions for federal criminal offenses.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner broker was employed by a bank at the time he was issued a real estate broker's license. Shortly thereafter, he participated in a bank transaction that resulted in his conviction for receiving a gift for aiding in procurement of a loan, conspiracy, and submitting false reports. Petitioner was fined and sentenced to one year imprisonment. The Real Estate Brokers Act of 1929 provided that where, during the term of any license, the licensee was found guilty of certain offenses including those involving the misrepresentation, larceny, or burglary of money or property, the real estate commission must revoke the license. 63 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 440(a), 441(b). Petitioner argued that the act should not be applied to him because his convictions were unrelated to the practice of real estate. In affirming the revocation of petitioner's license, the court ruled that petitioner's crimes involved substantial misrepresentation on his part and that the commission did not commit an abuse of discretion by revoking his license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of petitioner broker's real estate license by respondent real estate commission. The court ruled that a license revocation was appropriate solely by virtue of petitioner's conviction for crimes in violation of the Real Estate Brokers Act.

Shelley v. Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 1054 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


71 Pa. Commw. 153; 454 A.2d 664; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1216


November 18, 1982, Argued  
January 13, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.
Later proceeding at Ruby v. Carlisle Zoning Hearing Bd., 88 Pa. Commw. 70, 488 A.2d 655, 1985 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 862 (1985)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County in the case of William L. Shelley, W. L. Hall, Louis F. Del Duca, Charles W. Rogers and Georgette Rogers v. The Zoning Hearing Board of Carlisle, No. 1696-1980, and in the case of Constance B. Ruby, t/a Walnut Bottom Tavern v. The Zoning Hearing Board of Carlisle, No. 1783-1980.
Shelley v. Carlisle Zoning Hearing Bd., 18 Pa. D. & C.3d 337, 1981 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 489 (1981)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant neighbors sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed appellee zoning hearing board's decision to allow a tavern to be rebuilt after it had been damaged by fire.


OVERVIEW: After a fire damaged a tavern, appellee zoning hearing board concluded that the Carlisle, Pa., Zoning Ordinance, § 901, did not prohibit the reconstruction of the tavern, which was a nonconforming use in a residential district. Appellant neighbors challenged appellee's decision, and the trial court affirmed. Appellant neighbors challenged the decision, and the court reversed because the owner failed to properly challenge the validity of the Carlisle, Pa., Zoning Ordinance, § 901.1, and failed to request or introduce evidence that justified the granting of a variance under the Pennsylvania Municipalities Planning Code (PMPC), 53 P.S. § 10912. The owner's notice to the town that stated that the owner sought relief from a provision in a zoning ordinance did not constitute a challenge to the ordinance under PMPC, P.S. § 11004. The owner's attorney never requested a variance and did not present evidence that indicated that the owner was entitled to one under PMPC, 53 P.S. § 10912.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that affirmed appellee zoning hearing board's decision to allow a tavern to be rebuilt after it had been damaged by fire because the owner's letter to the town did not constitute a challenge to the validity of the zoning statute, and the owner failed to request a variance of present evidence that demonstrated that the owner was entitled to a variance.

 

948 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Edwards v. Commonwealth, State Dental Council & Examining Bd.


No. 1515 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


71 Pa. Commw. 139; 454 A.2d 218; 1983 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1201


November 16, 1982, Argued  
January 12, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Dental Council and Examining Board in case of In the Matter of the Suspension or Revocation of the License to Practice as a Dental Hygienist, No. 2891, issued June 22, 1966, to Susan Edwards, D.H., dated May 22, 1981.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner dental hygienist appealed from an order of respondent state dental council and examining board (Pennsylvania), which revoked petitioner's license to practice, pursuant to the dental law, 63 P.S. § 122(i), for performing dental hygiene services without the direct supervision of a licensed dentist.


OVERVIEW: Respondent state dental council and examining board revoked petitioner dental hygienist's license for performing dental hygiene services without a licensed dentist's direct supervision, pursuant to 63 P.S. § 122(i). Petitioner claimed that the law deprived her of due process as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court affirmed, and held that the property right to practice a profession was not an absolute vested right, and the practice of a profession can legitimately be regulated under a state's inherent police power. The law in this case was directed to safeguarding the public health, as part of the state's broad police powers because it insured that hygienists practice only the limited services, which their education has prepared them to perform. Thus, the law had a rational basis and was not oppressive or arbitrary. Nor did the law violate petitioner's rights under the equal protection clause because the provisions of the law applied equally to all persons engaged in the practice of dental hygiene, none of whom were subjected to restriction, or held entitled to privileges, different from those allowed any other hygienist.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent state dental council and examining board, which revoked petitioner dental hygienist's license to practice because petitioner failed to show that the statute under which her license was revoked unconstitutionally deprived her of due process rights nor did the law violate the equal protection clause.

Ohio Edison Co. v. Commonwealth


Nos. 2274 C.D. 1980, 2275 C.D. 1980, 2276 C.D. 1980, 2277 C.D. 1980, 2278 C.D. 1980, 2279 C.D. 1980, 2293 C.D. 1980, 2321 C.D. 1980, 2322 C.D. 1980, 2323 C.D. 1980, 2324 C.D. 1980, 2325 C.D. 1980, 2336 C.D. 1980, 2337 C.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


70 Pa. Commw. 343; 453 A.2d 50; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1818


June 3, 1981, Argued  
December 10, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Department of Revenue in the cases of Ohio Edison Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Pennsylvania Gas and Water Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Pennsylvania Power & Light Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; UGI Corporation v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Philadelphia Electric Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Pennsylvania Power Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Delmarva Power & Light Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Harvey Bartle, Attorney General of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Howard A. Cohen, Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Pennsylvania Electric Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Metropolitan Edison Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Public Service Electric & Gas Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Jersey Central Power & Light Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Atlantic City Electric Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; Allegheny County Steam Heating Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; and Duquesne Light Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Motions to quash denied and cases remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner utility companies sought review of the order of the Secretary of Revenue (Pennsylvania), which precluded petitioners from challenging the calculations made by respondent secretary of revenue in the imposition of a surtax upon petitioners.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner utility companies challenged a notice and certification issued by respondent secretary of revenue. Petitioners contended that because they were precluded from challenging the calculations made by respondent by way of the refund provisions of the fiscal code, that the notice and certification, without prior notice or hearing, constituted a violation of their due process rights. They argued that they were entitled to a remand for a hearing to ascertain the manner in which these calculations were made by respondent. The court reversed the order of the trial court and held that because respondent failed to present a strong reason why the government's interests required that this determination should have been made without notice or opportunity to be heard by petitioners, some type of minimal due process was required to protect petitioners' due process rights. Without an opportunity to at least submit questions and written objections to the calculation of this surtax, petitioners were precluded from receiving even a modicum of due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order of the secretary of revenue, which precluded petitioner utility companies from challenging the calculations made by respondent secretary of revenue in the imposition of a surtax upon petitioner. The court held that respondent's preclusion of petitioners' right to challenge the calculations of the surtax was inappropriate because it violated petitioners' due process rights.

White Advertising Metro, Inc. v. Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 2903 C.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


70 Pa. Commw. 308; 453 A.2d 29; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1737


June 7, 1982, Argued  
December 8, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County in the case of White Advertising Metro, Inc. and Robert and Mary Louise Klinger v. The Zoning Hearing Board of Susquehanna Township, No. 345 S 1979.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, individuals and advertising company, challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which denied judicial review of appellee zoning hearing board's decision denying appellants' application for conditional use permits. Appellants claimed that appellee abused its discretion and that the denial was not supported by the evidence adduced at the public hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, individuals and advertising company, applied for conditional use permits to construct three outdoor advertising signs in the township. Appellee zoning hearing board denied the application and appellants sought review. The court found that the proposed signs were properly maintained, posed no safety hazard or nuisance to neighbors through illumination, and were limited in size and location along the roadway, and that appellants satisfied the burden to prove a favorable result when the proposal was considered under the statutory review standards. The court found that those objecting, as a matter of law, could not rely on the lack of revenue-producing potential in the proposal to show general detriment to the health, safety or welfare of the community, and that appellee abused its discretion in basing its denial of the permit on subjective aesthetic judgments. The court reversed the decision of appellee and ordered that appellants' application be approved.


OUTCOME: The order of appellee zoning hearing board denying the application of appellants, individuals and advertising company, for a conditional use permit to construct three outdoor advertising signs was reversed because appellants complied with the zoning ordinance, appellee abused its discretion when it based its denial on a subjective aesthetic judgment, and objectors did not show harm to the public interest.

 

951 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Appeal of Kasorex


No. 506 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


70 Pa. Commw. 193; 452 A.2d 921; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1721


June 10, 1982, Argued  
December 1, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued October 5, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County in case of Appeal of Kasorex, a Partnership, from the decision of the Board of Supervisors of Montgomery Township, No. 80-11921.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Supervisors of Montgomery Township sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), in favor of appellee development partnership, ordering the issuance of the requested development approval upon the ground that the Montgomery Township Zoning Ordinance did not exist.


OVERVIEW: The Montgomery Township Zoning Ordinance previously was held unconstitutional for excluding mobile home parks. Appellee development partnership, claiming a right to build quadruplexes, argued, and the trial court agreed, that the prior decision nullified the entire zoning ordinance, leaving the municipality wholly without zoning, and that the invalidity could not cured by amendment, but only by reenacting the zoning. The court found little procedural difference between enactment of an original zoning ordinance and an amendment, where the valid land-use controls would remain to protect the rest of the municipality. Appellee's case rested on inapposite dictum that did not, by invalidating one use, deregulate all others. That authority cited by appellee questioned whether an exclusionary zoning ordinance could be amended by allowing the excluded use in a location other than the one as to which a challenger applied. The Pennsylvania Supreme Court had held only that municipalities could not "zone around" a successful challenger. The court, therefore, reversed the lower court's order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order in favor of appellee development partnership, which ordered the issuance of the requested development approval, and held that the Montgomery Township Zoning Ordinance, except for the provision that was previously invalidated for unlawfully excluding one class of residential use, did remain in existence and could be cured by amendment, because reenactment in its entirety was not required.

Briglia v. Commonwealth, Unemployment Compensation Bd. of Review


No. 1093 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


70 Pa. Commw. 159; 452 A.2d 900; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1710


June 11, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
November 23, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in case of In Re: Claim of Nicholas Briglia, No. B-194190.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant employee appealed a decision from respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the decision of a referee that denied unemployment compensation benefits as a result of claimant's financial ineligibility pursuant to the Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Law, 43 P.S. § 804(c).


OVERVIEW: Claimant employee appealed a decision from respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the decision of a referee that denied unemployment compensation benefits as a result of claimant's financial ineligibility pursuant to the Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Law, 43 P.S. § 804(c). The court affirmed and held that a determination of the number of credit weeks a claimant would have, a critical factor was the date on which the claimant filed his application for benefits. It is that date which determined a claimant's "benefit year" which in turn established the claimant's "base year." 43 P.S. §§ 753(g.1), 43 P.S. § 753(b).During the base year, claimant only had 16 credit weeks which fell short of the 18 credit weeks required by § 804(c). The court further held that the statute was not applied retroactively, as claimant's application was made after the effective date of the statute under which applications would be processed, and this was insufficient to have characterized the application of the amendment as retroactive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision from respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the decision of a referee that denied unemployment compensation benefits as a result of claimant employee's financial ineligibility. Claimant failed to establish the required minimum 18 credit weeks.

Bonzer v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Environmental Resources


No. 549 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


69 Pa. Commw. 633; 452 A.2d 280; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1686


September 15, 1982, Argued  
November 10, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Environmental Hearing Board in the case of Charles J. Bonzer v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Docket No. 80-033-B.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowner appealed from the order of respondent Environmental Hearing Board (Pennsylvania), which upheld an order of the Department of Environmental Resources requiring petitioner, at his own expense, to make repairs to a system of storm water culverts and a watercourse located on his property.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Environmental Resources (DER) determined that petitioner landowner violated the Dam Safety and Encroachment Act, 32 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 693.5, and ordered him to make certain repairs to collapsed culverts and the watercourse on his property within 30 days. The order of DER was upheld by respondent Environmental Hearing Board. On appeal, the court reversed respondent's order of in part, and affirmed in part. The court held that the DER's finding that the condition of petitioner's property was causally related to the flooding was adequately supported by testimony. However, the court found that 25 Pa. Code § 105 did not evince an intent to require the private owner of a bridge or culvert to do any more than completely remove a collapsed structure from the watercourse. Because the corrective actions that were ordered by DER exceeded that required by § 105, the court reversed the DER's order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed respondent Environmental Hearing Board's order affirming the decision of the Department of Environmental Resources (DER), which required that petitioner landowner repair storm water culverts on his property. The court held that the applicable regulations required only that petitioner remove the collapsed structures from the watercourse, and DER did not have authority to require petitioner to do more than what was required.

Bell Tel. Co. v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


No. 1637 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


69 Pa. Commw. 554; 452 A.2d 86; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1661


September 13, 1982, Argued  
November 5, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission in the case of Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission v. The Bell Telephone Company of Pennsylvania, No. R-80061235.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner utility appealed from the order of respondent Public Utility Commission (Pennsylvania), which delayed petitioner's receipt of rate relief for 21 days.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner utility filed revised tariffs with respondent Public Utility Commission that were designed to increase its annual operating revenues. Respondent determined that a smaller rate increase was necessary, and ordered petitioner to file revised tariffs. Respondent later issued an order delaying the rate increase for 21 days. On appeal, the court held that the Public Utility Code (Code), 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1302-1303 (1976), did not prohibit respondent from ordering retroactive rate relief. The court held that there was nothing in the Code to support the 21-day delay in the receipt of rate relief following PUC's determination that an increase was needed. Finally, the court held that the delay in the receipt of increased revenues that were found to be necessary, at a time when petitioner was producing compliance tariffs and required supportive materials, appeared to have violated 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1308(d). Thus, the court modified the order of PUC to provide an earlier effective date for the approved rates, and affirmed the order as modified.


OUTCOME: The court modified respondent Public Utility Commission's order, which delayed petitioner utility's receipt of an approved rate increase, and affirmed as modified. The court held that respondent was not barred from ordering retroactive rate relief, that the 21-day delay in petitioner's receipt of the approved rate increased was not warranted, and that the delay appeared to have violated applicable provisions of the Public Utility Code.

Einsing v. Pennsylvania Mines Corp.


No. 2272 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


69 Pa. Commw. 351; 452 A.2d 558; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1620; 70 Oil & Gas Rep. 554


October 5, 1982, Argued  
October 18, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Environmental Hearing Board in the case of Pennsylvania Mines Corporation v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Environmental Resources and Barry D. Einsig, Permittee, Docket No. 82-176-G.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Permit reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner oil driller sought review of the order of the Environmental Hearing Board (Pennsylvania), which revoked a permit that was granted to petitioner by the Department of Environmental Resources to drill a well through a coal mine owned by respondent mining company.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner oil driller was granted a permit by the Department of Environmental Resources (DER) to drill a well through a coal mine owned by respondent mining company. Respondent filed an appeal with the Environmental Hearings Board (board). The board voided the permit on the ground that the issuance of the permit constituted an abuse of discretion on the part of DER. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the board, holding that the findings of fact did not support the conclusion that petitioner's well would have unduly interfered with or endangered the mine, in violation of the Gas Operations Well-Drilling Petroleum and Coal Mining Act (Act), 52 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2202(b) (1955). The court held that the effect of the board's decision would have been to render petitioner's estate in the land, the right to drill for oil and gas, non-existent and would have deprived petitioner of the lawful use of his property. Finally, the court held that the test formulated by the board to establish whether a well would have interfered with or endangered a mine did not reflect the intent of the legislature when it passed the Act and that it was susceptible to confiscatory application.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the Environmental Hearing Board (board) voiding the permit granted to petitioner oil driller to drill a well through a coal mine owned by respondent mining company. The court held that the board's conclusion of law did not flow from its findings of fact, and that the board's interpretation of the Gas Operations Well-Drilling Petroleum and Coal Mining Act was confiscatory in its application.

Cochran v. Commonwealth


No. 64 T.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


69 Pa. Commw. 74; 450 A.2d 756; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1575


June 8, 1982, Argued  
September 16, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County in the case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Patricia A. Cochran, Nos. 258 and 260 Misc. Dkt. 1980.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a retail sales employee in a store, sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which convicted her of violating Doylestown Borough, Pa., Ordinance No. 1980-5 (May 9, 1980), for selling or offering to sell drug paraphernalia.


OVERVIEW: While working as a retails sales employee at a store, defendant was cited for, and convicted of, violating Doylestown Borough, Pa., Ordinance No. 1980-5 (May 9, 1980), by selling or offering to sell drug paraphernalia. Defendant sought review of her conviction on the grounds that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague, that her conviction violated her due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 because it was based on intent transferred from remote third party manufacturers, and that her trial counsel was ineffective as a matter of law. The court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that the ordinance was not vague as applied to defendant because the items she was charged with selling fell clearly within the definition of "drug paraphernalia" and the ordinance required that the trier of fact find that she sold the items knowing they would be used in conjunction with prohibited controlled substances. The court also found that defendant's conviction was based upon her own intent, not a transferred intent, and that her trial counsel was not ineffective because the issues that defendant argued that her counsel failed to make were meritless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, convicting defendant of selling or offering to sale drug paraphernalia, because the court found that the ordinance was not vague because the items defendant was found to be selling fell squarely within the definition of drug paraphernalia and the ordinance contained a specific intent requirement.

Moyer's Landfill v. Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 1741 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


69 Pa. Commw. 47; 450 A.2d 273; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1565; 13 ELR 20438


June 8, 1982, Argued  
September 14, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County in the case of Moyer's Landfill, Inc. v. Zoning Hearing Board of Lower Providence Township, No. 78-11852.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which upheld respondent zoning hearing board's decision denying appellant approval to use his land as a sanitary landfill. Respondent challenged the trial court's order reversing respondent's decision that appellant was required to pay the fees of a lawyer and engineer employed by the township in opposing appellant's application.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowner operated a landfill as a non-conforming-use that was established prior to a zoning ordinance that prohibited the use of any land in the township as a landfill. Appellant petitioned respondent zoning hearing board for approval to use an adjoining tract of land as sanitary landfill. Respondent denied the request; however, it amended the ordinance to permit landfills when authorized as a special exception. Appellant challenged the trial court's decision which affirmed respondent's denial of a zoning permit and special exception, while respondent challenged an order reversing its order that appellant pay the fees for an attorney and engineer hired by the township to oppose appellant's applications. The court affirmed the trial court's order as to the fees; however, it reversed the trial court's decision regarding appellant's applications. The court found that the ordinance had unconstitutionally banned a legitimate business use of land because the ban was not sufficiently related to issues of health and safety. The court also found that appellant was entitled to the special exception because respondent's reasons for rejecting the application were insufficient.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision affirming respondent zoning hearing board's decision denying appellant landowner's application for a zoning permit and special exception because the court found that an ordinance that had banned landfills in the township was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court's order reversing respondent's order that appellant pay fees incurred by the township while opposing his applications.

Paradise v. Mt. Airy Lodge, Inc.


No. 1336 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


68 Pa. Commw. 548; 449 A.2d 849; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1523


June 8, 1982, Argued  
September 1, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Monroe County in cases of Township of Paradise v. Mt. Airy Lodge, Inc., 788 June Term, 1979, and Mt. Airy Lodge, Inc. v. Zoning Hearing Board of Paradise Township and Township of Paradise, No. 2525 of 1980.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Monroe County (Pennsylvania), which denied its appeal from a cease and desist order issued under appellee township's zoning ordinance, which required appellant to stop excavating shale from its property because that particular land use was prohibited on any land within the township.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowner had a tract of land in appellee township that contained three shale pits. Appellant actively excavated shale from one of the pits, primarily, but not solely, for its own use. Pursuant to the local zoning ordinance that prohibited shale excavation on any land in the township, a cease and desist order was issued and appellant sought review of the trial court's decision which denied its appeal from the order. The court reversed the trial court's decision because the court found that the ordinance was exclusionary because it totally prohibited a legitimate business use of appellant's land and appellee was unable to demonstrate that the ban bore a sufficiently substantial relationship to the public health, safety, morals, and general welfare to justify the prohibition. The court found that the ordinance was not prima facie valid because it totally excluded the excavation of shale, therefore, the court focused on the purpose of the ban to determine the validity of the ordinance. The court held that the concerns regarding the adverse impact on tourism and noise and vibrations from blasting were unfounded and insufficient to justify the ban.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision denying appellant landowner's appeal of a cease and desist order because appellant township's zoning ordinance was exclusionary. The ordinance totally banned a legitimate business use of the land without a sufficiently substantial relationship to the public health, safety, and general welfare.

Sto-Rox School Dist. v. Horgan


Nos. 456 C.D. 1981, 538 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


68 Pa. Commw. 416; 449 A.2d 796; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1511


October 7, 1981, Argued  
August 26, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in case of Sandra L. Horgan, Gloria Ann Postcavage, John Suszynski, Howard Duerr, William Palmero, Jeffrey Kunzelman, Eugene Chieffo, Mark Roman, Glen Bednar, Carolyn T. Lee, Victor Janosick, Thaddeus P. Chiechenowski, Valeri Kinlan, Gregory Sembrat, Kenneth Slish and Inez Ferchak v. Sto-Rox School District, No. SA 905 of 1980.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part. Case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district and appellee teachers both challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which upheld in part the action by appellant suspending appellees for the 1978-1979 school year.


OVERVIEW: Appellant school district passed a resolution suspending appellee teachers from their positions in the secondary schools due to a substantial decline in student enrollment. Both parties challenged the trial court's order which upheld that action only in part. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. It affirmed to the extent that appellees were not denied due process, because they were not entitled to preliminary hearings prior to suspension. The court reversed, however, to the extent that the trial court applied an incorrect statute in evaluating the criteria underlying the choice of which teachers to suspend. The action was governed by 24 P.S. § 1125(b) rather than a later statutory provision, because the law to be applied was that in effect on the date of the suspension, not the date of the adjudication. As the trial court applied the later law in assessing claims, the case was remanded for appropriate determinations under the law in effect on the date that appellees were suspended.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part in the dispute between appellee teachers and appellant school district. The court upheld the trial court's decision that due process principles did not require grant of a hearing to appellees prior to their suspension based on declining enrollments. But, the case was remanded, as the wrong law was applied in assessing the statutory criteria for determining who should be suspended.

Adams County v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Public Welfare


No. 2116 C.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


68 Pa. Commw. 249; 448 A.2d 1202; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1456


June 3, 1981, Argued  
August 11, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued February 2, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original jurisdiction in the case of Adams County et al. v. Department of Public Welfare of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and Honorable Helen B. O'Bannon, Secretary of the Department of Public Welfare.



DISPOSITION: Motion for summary judgment of petitioners granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, counties, filed a motion for summary judgment in their action against respondents, department of public welfare and its secretary, that sought full reimbursement for expenditures associated with child welfare services under Act 148, 62 P.S. § 704.1. Respondents also filed a motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Act 148, 62 P.S. § 704.1, respondents, department of public welfare and its secretary, were to reimburse petitioners, counties, for the expenditures associated with child welfare services. Respondents informed petitioners that the appropriations for the child welfare services were insufficient to meet petitioners' expenditures in the fiscal year. Petitioners initiated an action against respondents that sought enforcement of Act 148. Petitioners' application for preliminary injunction was denied and both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The court granted petitioners' motion for summary judgment because under Act 148, respondents were required to make the reimbursements. The court found that respondents had approved petitioners' child welfare plans prior to requesting the appropriation from the commonwealth and, therefore, abused its discretion when it failed to request the necessary funds. The court held that respondents had a ministerial duty to request the sufficient funds to cover the costs of the programs. The court denied respondents' motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioners', counties, motion for summary judgment in its action that sought full reimbursement for child welfare programs from respondents, department of public welfare and its secretary, because respondents were required to request the necessary funds from the commonwealth under Act 148. The court denied respondents' motion for summary judgment.

 

962 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Lewis v. Thornburgh


No. 2535 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


68 Pa. Commw. 157; 448 A.2d 680; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1468


June 8, 1982, Argued  
August 5, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of H. Craig Lewis, State Senator v. Governor Richard Thornburgh and Jay Waldman.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained in part and overruled in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner senator sought specific relief in the form of an order directing respondents, governor and general counsel, to provide petitioner with data characterized by the petition as "budgetary information."


OVERVIEW: Petitioner senator sought an order directing respondents, governor and general counsel, to supply him with budgetary data. Exercising its original jurisdiction, the court sustained respondents' objections to the first count of the petition, finding that citizens are afforded only the right to extract or copy public records and have no right to demand that information be assembled and transmitted. In addition, the court found it did not have original jurisdiction in this matter. The court overruled respondents' objections to the second count of the petition, finding that the matter was justiciable and that the information requested was clearly budgetary data and that all petitioner was requesting was that a constitutional and statutory duty of a routine nature be performed by respondents.


OUTCOME: The court sustained respondents' objections to the first count of the petition, finding that the court did not have jurisdiction in the matter. However, the court overruled the objections to count two of the petition because the matter was justiciable and the data sought was clearly budgetary in nature.

 

963 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


In re Street


No. 1403 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


67 Pa. Commw. 441; 447 A.2d 1052; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1405


July 1, 1982, Heard  
July 15, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of In Re: Nomination Certificate of T. Milton Street as Republican Candidate for the Office of Representative in Congress From the Second Congressional District -- Objection of William H. Gray, III.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted. Secretary ordered not to certify name of candidate.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent political party committeemen challenged the claim filed in the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania by petitioner congressman to set aside respondents' substitute nomination certificate on grounds that their candidate's name could not be barred from appearing twice on the ballot for the same office because the provision in the Pennsylvania Election Code that prohibited this, 25 P.S. § 2939, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner congressman filed an action that sought to set aside respondent political party committeemen's substitute nomination certificate of their party's new candidate for Congress after respondents' original candidate dropped out of the race. This new candidate already appeared on the ballot as a candidate for a different political party. The Pennsylvania Election Code, 25 P.S. § 2939, prohibited a political party from filing a substitute nomination certificate that nominated any person who had already been nominated by another political party or political body for the same office. Respondents argued that § 2939 violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV in that it discriminated in favor of major political parties and violated respondents' rights to engage in political association. The court held that the statute was constitutional because all that had been denied to respondents and their candidate was double access to the ballot, which right was not constitutionally protected.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner congressman's request and ordered the Secretary of the Commonwealth to set aside the substitute nomination certificate that sought to include respondent political party committeemen's candidate on the ballot. The court held that a candidate may not appear twice on a ballot for the same office and found that respondents' candidate already appeared on the ballot for a different political party.

 

964 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Allegheny Ludlum Steel Corp. v. Pa. Public Util. Com


Nos. 242 C.D. 1982, 257 C.D. 1982


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


67 Pa. Commw. 400; 447 A.2d 675; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1379


May 4, 1982, Argued  
July 13, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission in cases of Freedom Forge Corporation, t/d/b/a Standard Steel v. Pennsylvania Electric Company, Docket No. M-810294C008 and Allegheny Ludlum Steel Corporation v. West Penn Power Company, Docket No. M-810294C004 and Original Jurisdiction No. 3159 C.D. 1981, in the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania in case of Allegheny Ludlum Steel Corporation v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission.



DISPOSITION: Motions to quash appeals granted. Preliminary objections to petition for declaratory judgment overruled in part and sustained in part. Action dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner steel corporation filed suit for a declaratory judgment against respondent state public utility commission, claiming that its approval of an energy cost rate (ECR), 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1307, adjustment given to an electric power company was unconstitutional on the ground that the ECR failed to afford procedural due process. Respondent objected to the lawsuit, arguing that the court was without jurisdiction to hear the suit.


OVERVIEW: Respondent state public utility commission gave approval to an electric power company's request for an energy cost rate (ECR) under 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1307. Petitioner steel corporation filed suit seeking a declaratory judgment against respondent, arguing that § 1307 was unconstitutional on the ground that it failed to afford procedural due process. Respondent filed a demurrer, arguing that the court was without jurisdiction to hear the lawsuit. The court held that a declaratory judgment was the proper procedure to determine whether a statute violates the constitutional rights of those whom the statute affects, however, the court should refuse declaratory relief if the controversy at issue can be resolved by alternative means. The court determined that petitioner had a option to administrative seek review of the ECR after it has been approved by seeking a refund with interest. The court stated that because petitioner had a remedy, the court was without jurisdiction to grant declaratory relief. The court sustained the demurrer in respondent's preliminary objection and dismissed the lawsuit because the court was without jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed petitioner steel corporation's lawsuit for declaratory judgment because it was without jurisdiction to consider the matter because petitioner had a administrative appeal option available after respondent state public utility commission approved an energy cost rate for an electric power company.

Lisa H. v. State Bd. of Educ.


No. 54 T.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


67 Pa. Commw. 350; 447 A.2d 669; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1373


December 16, 1981, Argued  
July 8, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County in the case of Lisa Applebaum and Nicole Applebaum, minors, by Doris Applebaum, their mother and natural guardian v. Bensalem Township School District, Robert H. Hays, Individually and in his capacity as District Superintendent of the Bensalem Township School District, Thomas P. Waters, Individually and in his capacity as Director of Elementary Education, Joseph S. Stroman, Individually and in his capacity as Early Childhood Education Supervisor, William Snyder, Individually and in his capacity as Director of Secondary Education, Bensalem Township School Board, David G. Costello, Individually and in his capacity as President of the Bensalem Township School Board, Robert A. Carr, Individually and in his capacities as Accountant for the Bensalem Township School District and Treasurer of the Bensalem Township School Board, Bucks County Intermediate Unit, George Rabb, Individually and in his capacity as Executive Director of the Bucks County Intermediate Unit, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Education, Robert G. Scanlon, Individually and in his capacity [***2] as Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Education, The State Board of Education of the Commonwealth, John Hershey, Individually and in his capacity as Executive Director of the State Board of Education of the Commonwealth, No. 80-8650-10-5, dated September 16, 1980.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained and case dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant educators filed preliminary objections in the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania to plaintiff parent's claim for equitable relief that arose from defendants' decision that plaintiff's children could not participate in gifted and talented school programs pursuant to the State Board of Education Regulations as such children were defined in 22 Pa. Code § 13.1(ii).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff parent challenged the decision of defendant educators to exclude plaintiff's children from gifted and talented school programs on grounds that these programs violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV and the Pennsylvania constitution. Defendants filed preliminary objections against plaintiff's claims. The court sustained defendants' objections and dismissed plaintiff's claims. The court held that plaintiff failed to state a cause of action because she did not claim that her children qualified as "gifted and talented school-aged persons" under 22 Pa. Code. § 13.1(ii) or that her children were ever denied the right to be evaluated or considered for admission to the program. The court also held that plaintiff did not have standing for these same reasons and that an adequate remedy at law existed because plaintiff had the right to present written evidence that her children qualified for the program and to seek admission of her children into the program.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed plaintiff parent's claim against defendant educators. The court held that specialized education only for children who deviate from the norm could exist because such is reasonably related to a thorough and efficient system of public education, that plaintiff did not have standing because she did not allege that her children qualified for the program, and that equity did not lie because plaintiff could apply for the program.

Official Court Reporters of Court of Common Pleas v. Pennsylvania Labor Relations Bd.


No. 430 C.D. 1981


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


67 Pa. Commw. 256; 446 A.2d 1357; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1362


March 2, 1982, Argued  
June 30, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument and Reconsideration Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in case of Official Court Reporters of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County v. Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board, American Federation of State, County and Municipal Employees; Board of Judges, Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County; and Court Administrator of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, No. 901 April Term, 1979.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Order of Board dated July 30, 1975 reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant association of court reporters sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an order of appellee, the Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board, vacating its prior order of certification in favor of appellee union and setting aside appellee union's prior petition for representation.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, court judges and the state labor relations board, argued that appellant court reporters association lacked standing to challenge appellee board's order decertifying appellee union as appellant's representative because it was not a party to the decertification proceeding. Disagreeing, the court observed that 2 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 702 granted a right of appeal to any person "aggrieved" by an state agency action even though the person was not a "party" within the meaning of Pa. R. App. P. 501. Appellant was aggrieved in being denied the right to bargain as a homogeneous unit, the court added, as it had a substantial, direct, and immediate interest in appellee board's action. The court then rejected appellant's contention that the res judicata and law-of-the-case doctrines barred appellee board from reconsidering its prior finding of unit appropriateness. However, the court agreed that appellee board exceeded the scope of a state supreme court remand order, which merely directed it to identify the employer authorized to bargain with appellee union, rather than to reconsider its original certification order, which it could not do absent a petition for reconsideration.


OUTCOME: Order of appellee labor relations board vacating its prior order of certification in favor of appellee union reversed, and certification order reinstated, because appellant court reporters association had standing to challenge appellee board's decertification order, as it was a party aggrieved by state agency action, and because appellee board exceeded the scope of a remand order limiting it to identifying the employer authorized to bargain.

 

967 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Lapp v. County of Chester


No. 2411 C.D. 1980


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


67 Pa. Commw. 86; 445 A.2d 1356; 1982 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1329


March 2, 1982, Argued  
June 4, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County in case of Isaac L. Lapp and Ruth A. Lapp, his wife v. County of Chester Tax Claim Bureau and Tom Swift, No. 302-P-8 Misc. Term, 1979.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, husband and wife, challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania) denying their petition to set aside a tax sale made by appellee county to appellee purchaser. Appellants contended that they received insufficient notice pursuant to § 602 of the Real Estate Tax Sale Law, 72 P.S. § 5860.602 and an inadequate price.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, husband and wife, filed a petition to set aside the tax sale, conducted by appellee county, of their former real estate by contending that they were not afforded the notice required by § 602 of the Real Estate Tax Sale Law, 72 P.S. § 5860.602, and that appellee purchaser paid an inadequate purchase price at the tax sale. The court affirmed the trial court order denying appellant's petition on both grounds. The court ruled that the precedent appellants invoked regarding the mail notice issue was inapplicable. The trial court correctly found that appellants failed to rebut the prima facie presumption of the regularity of the acts of public officers after the deputy sheriff scotch taped the notice of intended sale in a conspicuous place on the door of appellants' premises. The court found that the case law cited by appellants to contend that the purchase price was inadequate and to set aside the sale were inapplicable. The court ruled that a statutorily satisfactory price afforded no grounds to prove unjust enrichment to set aside a sale. The court confirmed the sale of appellants' property after concluding that it occurred according to the provisions of § 5860.602.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order that denied the petition of appellants, husband and wife, to set aside the tax sale appellee county made to appellee purchaser. The court did not find that appellants received insufficient statutory notice, but they failed to rebut the presumption of the regularity of the acts of a public officer. The court did not evaluate the adequacy of the purchase price because the sale occurred according to the law.
